Do the agent instruction in the message as per your agent number.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 13:56:49)

_Thought for a few seconds_

## Agent 2 / B — Zero-side actual-zeta anti-design obstruction

### Task

Attack Gate 1 from the zero side. The current architecture has converged to the thesis that smooth Gate 2 is local analysis, while singular Gate 2 reduces to the same Gate 1 anti-quadrature obstruction in rescaled variables. The main missing theorem is therefore actual-zeta source-curvature observability:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The prompt asks whether actual zeta zero geometry can rule out the same-scale finite-jet quadrature adversary. 

---

# 1. Same-scale packet coordinates

Use the local packet scale \(d\). A packet centered near the relevant ordinate is represented by

\[
x_j=d\cos\theta_j,\qquad c_j=d\sin\theta_j,
\qquad 0<\theta_j<\pi,
\]

where \(x_j\) is the horizontal displacement in the rescaled ordinate coordinate and \(c_j\) is the packet denominator depth.

Set

\[
m=m_0+d u.
\]

A normalized same-scale kernel has the form

\[
K_{\theta}(u)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(u-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

A finite cluster gives

\[
Q(u)=\sum_{j=1}^N w_j K_{\theta_j}(u),
\qquad w_j>0
\]

in the positive-packet model.

The singular/shallow regime is identical after rescaling

\[
m=\gamma+c u.
\]

Then near packets with

\[
\Delta_{\nu_j}\asymp c
\]

give the same normalized model, with \(d\) replaced by \(c\). The singular powers of \(c^{-1}\) factor out and do not change the finite-jet algebra.

---

# 2. Source-flattening moment equations

The decisive local no-go model is the continuous positive same-scale distribution

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]

It produces a constant aggregate profile near the midpoint:

\[
Q_\mu(u)=\int K_\theta(u)\,d\mu(\theta)=\frac{1}{d}
\]

in the original scale, or simply a constant in normalized variables. Therefore

\[
Q_\mu^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad r\ge1.
\]

Finite quadrature replaces \(d\mu\) by finitely many positive nodes:

\[
Q_N(u)=\sum_{j=1}^N w_jK_{\theta_j}(u),
\]

matching derivatives through finite order:

\[
Q_N^{(r)}(0)=0,
\qquad 1\le r\le R.
\]

For source-curvature flatness, the minimum relevant equations are the even-jet conditions

\[
Q_N''(0)=0,\qquad Q_N^{(4)}(0)=0,\qquad \ldots,\qquad Q_N^{(2M)}(0)=0.
\]

Equivalently, in the trigonometric parametrization, these become moment equations of the form

\[
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j P_k(\cos\theta_j,\sin\theta_j)=0,
\qquad 1\le k\le M,
\]

where \(P_k\) is the normalized \(2k\)-jet polynomial. In the harmonic basis used by the continuous measure, this can be expressed schematically as

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin((2k+1)\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad 1\le k\le M,
\]

up to the exact normalization of the kernel. The important point is not the specific trigonometric basis; it is that source flattening is a finite positive quadrature/moment system on the same-scale packet angles.

---

# 3. Number of packets needed

A positive quadrature formula matching \(M\) independent moment conditions needs

\[
N_M=O(M)
\]

nodes. More precisely, by Tchakaloff/Carathéodory-type finite quadrature, a measure matching \(M\) moments can be replaced by a positive atomic measure with at most

\[
M+1
\]

or \(O(M)\) atoms, depending on whether value normalization is included.

For Gate 1 interval flatness on

\[
|I_\rho|\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

the previous finite-jet scale audit suggests

\[
M\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively

\[
M=O(\log Q).
\]

Thus the quadrature adversary only requires

\[
N_M=O\!\left(\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right)
\]

or at worst

\[
N_M=O(\log Q)
\]

same-scale packets.

This is small enough that crude zero counting does **not** rule it out.

---

# 4. Comparison with local zero counting

A local Riemann–von Mangoldt estimate gives

\[
N(T+H)-N(T-H)\ll (H+1)\log T.
\]

On a \(Q^{-1}\)-scale height window, assuming \(Q\asymp \log T\), this gives

\[
N(T+Q^{-1})-N(T-Q^{-1})\ll 1+\frac{\log T}{Q}\asymp O(1)
\]

for a single narrow window, but the relevant same-scale packets need not all lie in exactly the same tiny real-ordinate interval if the packet model includes horizontal/off-critical depth and nearby auxiliary packets over the enlarged core. On a polynomially enlarged window, the bound is

\[
O(Q^C)
\]

which is vastly larger than \(O(\log Q)\).

So zero counting alone gives no contradiction. It can say the cluster is finite and polynomially bounded, but it does not forbid the \(O(M)\) packets needed for finite quadrature.

---

# 5. Candidate actual-zeta blockers

## 5.1 Riemann–von Mangoldt local counting

Local zero counting controls only cardinality:

\[
\#\{\rho:\gamma_\rho\in J\}\ll (|J|+1)\log T.
\]

It does not control angular placement in the same-scale packet variables

\[
(\cos\theta_j,\sin\theta_j)
\]

or the moment vector

\[
\left(P_1(\theta_j),\ldots,P_M(\theta_j)\right).
\]

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{not enough.}}
\]

---

## 5.2 Zero-density estimates off the critical line

Zero-density theorems bound the number of zeros with

\[
\Re\rho\ge \sigma
\]

in large height ranges. They are too coarse for a local packet quadrature problem. The quadrature adversary can use only \(O(M)\) packets, and \(M\) is logarithmic or sublogarithmic in \(Q\).

A density theorem would need to exclude even a small same-scale off-line packet configuration near the hypothetical \(\rho\). Known density estimates do not provide this.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{not enough unless upgraded to a local same-scale angular distribution theorem.}}
\]

---

## 5.3 Pair correlation / spacing

Pair correlation concerns critical-line zero ordinates, typically at average spacing scale

\[
\asymp \frac{1}{\log T}.
\]

The quadrature conditions are not merely spacing conditions. They require a finite moment design in a two-parameter packet space: ordinate displacement and denominator depth.

Even strong pair-correlation information would not directly forbid finitely many zeros from occupying quadrature-compatible positions. It might reduce the plausibility of some clusters, but it does not yield a deterministic exclusion.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{diagnostic only; not a proof.}}
\]

---

## 5.4 Quartet symmetry

Functional-equation quartet symmetry maps

\[
\rho\mapsto \bar\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

This enforces symmetric packet partners. But the known same-scale positive quadrature model already tolerates symmetric positive packet arrangements. Quartet closure changes the allowed node set and doubles/multiplies contributions, but it does not destroy the moment-design mechanism.

In fact, symmetry can make some odd moments vanish automatically, which may help rather than hurt cancellation.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{not enough; may assist cancellation.}}
\]

---

## 5.5 Simplicity of zeros

Simplicity prevents multiplicity at the same exact point. It does not prevent multiple nearby simple zeros from approximating a positive atomic quadrature measure.

Finite quadrature uses distinct nodes anyway, so simplicity is compatible with the adversary.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{not enough.}}
\]

---

## 5.6 Functional equation

The functional equation enforces the quartet symmetry above and contributes gamma/background terms. It does not, by itself, prevent finite same-scale packet designs. The hardened finite \(\xi\)-like countermodels already survive quartet symmetry and gamma/background hardening in the project’s ledger.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{not enough locally.}}
\]

---

# 6. Ordinary versus singular scale

The singular scale does not create a different zero-side obstruction.

If

\[
m=\gamma+c u,
\]

then a same-scale cluster with

\[
\Delta_{\nu_j}\asymp c
\]

has normalized profile

\[
Q(u)=\sum_j w_jK_{\eta_j,\xi_j}(u),
\]

and

\[
q^{(r)}(m)\sim c^{-(r+1)}Q^{(r)}(u).
\]

The large powers of \(c^{-1}\) factor out. To make source curvature small, one needs

\[
Q''(u)\approx0
\]

and higher finite jets small, exactly as in the ordinary scale.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular cancellation is the same same-scale quadrature problem in rescaled variables.}
}
\]

---

# 7. What actual zeta would need to forbid

Actual zeta must forbid a finite packet design of the following kind.

At any hypothetical off-line packet interval \(I_\rho\), after choosing the relevant local scale \(d\) or \(c\), the nearby actual zeta packets cannot satisfy

\[
\sum_j w_j K_{\theta_j}^{(r)}(0)
\approx 0
\]

for the finite derivative set needed to force interval source flatness, while maintaining

\[
q_0>0
\]

and the admissible good-patch conditions.

A precise missing theorem is:

**No same-scale source-flattening quadrature for actual zeta zeros.**  
Let \(I_\rho\) be an admissible packet interval associated with a hypothetical off-line packet. Let \(s\) be the relevant same-scale denominator, either ordinary or singular, and rescale \(m=m_0+s u\). Let the nearby actual zeta packets produce the normalized profile

\[
Q_{\near}(u)=\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal L_s} w_\nu K_\nu(u)+Q_{\mathrm{bg}}(u).
\]

Then for some fixed \(B\),

\[
\int_{|u|\lesssim |I_\rho|/s}
|Q_{\near}''(u)|^2\,du
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

in the normalization corresponding to

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Equivalently, in finite-jet form,

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
Q_{\near}^{(r+2)}(u_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

for

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or a conservative \(R(Q)=O(\log Q)\).

This theorem must use actual-zeta arithmetic, not just local zero geometry.

---

# 8. Does any known zero-side theorem prove it?

I do not see one.

Known zero-side inputs give:

\[
\text{cardinality bounds},
\]

\[
\text{symmetry constraints},
\]

\[
\text{coarse off-line density bounds},
\]

\[
\text{spacing statistics or conjectures},
\]

but not a deterministic finite-design exclusion of the form:

\[
\text{actual zeta zeros cannot match a prescribed same-scale quadrature moment vector.}
\]

Thus the zero-side route does not currently close Gate 1.

---

# 9. Final answer

The zero-side analysis gives a precise obstruction, but not a proof.

The obstruction is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{same-scale finite-jet quadrature by actual zeta packets.}
}
\]

Local packet geometry allows it. Quartet symmetry, simplicity, Riemann–von Mangoldt counting, pair correlation, and standard zero-density estimates do not appear to forbid it at polynomial precision.

So the missing zero-side theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta zeros cannot form a same-scale positive packet quadrature
matching source-curvature jets through }R(Q)\text{ orders.}
}
\]

Absent such a theorem, Gate 1 must likely be attacked from the prime/AFE fixed-coefficient side or by a genuinely global trace/explicit-formula argument rather than by zero-side local constraints alone.

I’ll answer as Agent 2/B. I’ll make the zero-side obstruction as explicit as possible: exact derivative/moment equations, packet count, and which known zero-side facts fail to exclude the design.

## Agent 2 / B — Zero-side anti-quadrature theorem

### Assignment

I am executing the Agent 2/B prompt: attack Gate 1 from the zero side. The current shared background states that the proof architecture now depends primarily on Gate 1, and that local zero geometry permits same-scale finite-jet quadrature unless actual-zeta arithmetic forbids it. 

Gate 1 is:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

The zero-side question is whether actual zeta zeros can realize a same-scale packet design that makes

\[
q''_{\can}
\]

flat on \(I_\rho\).

---

# 1. Normalized same-scale packet model

Use the normalized same-scale coordinates

\[
x_j=\cos\theta_j,\qquad c_j=\sin\theta_j,
\qquad 0<\theta_j<\pi.
\]

The normalized packet kernel is

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

Equivalently, since

\[
z_\theta=e^{i\theta},
\]

we have

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\Im\frac{1}{x-z_\theta}.
\]

A finite same-scale packet cluster is

\[
Q(x)=\sum_{j=1}^N w_jK_{\theta_j}(x),
\qquad w_j>0.
\]

This model covers both ordinary and singular scales after rescaling

\[
m=m_0+\lambda x,
\qquad \lambda=d \text{ or } c.
\]

The scale factor \(\lambda\) only contributes powers to derivatives; the normalized moment equations are the same.

---

# 2. Exact moment equations

At \(x=0\),

\[
\frac{d^n}{dx^n}\frac{1}{x-z}
=
(-1)^n n!(x-z)^{-n-1}.
\]

For \(z=e^{i\theta}\), this gives

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)
=
n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
\]

Hence

\[
Q^{(n)}(0)
=
n!\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin((n+1)\theta_j).
\]

Source flatness through order \(R+2\) requires

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,
\quad
Q^{(3)}(0)\approx0,
\quad
\ldots,
\quad
Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

If one also wants the aggregate profile centered and stationary, one may additionally impose

\[
Q'(0)\approx0,
\]

which is

\[
\sum_j w_j\sin(2\theta_j)\approx0.
\]

The value condition is not zero:

\[
Q(0)
=
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j
>0.
\]

So the finite-jet quadrature adversary is exactly:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0
\quad(k=2,3,\ldots,R+3),
\qquad
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j>0.
}
\]

For even source-curvature flattening only, one may restrict to

\[
Q^{(2\ell)}(0)=0,
\qquad
1\le \ell\le M,
\]

which gives

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin((2\ell+1)\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
1\le \ell\le M.
}
\]

This is the moment system referenced in the coordinator prompt.

---

# 3. Continuous positive quadrature model

The continuous measure

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta
\]

on \((0,\pi)\) produces a constant same-scale aggregate near \(x=0\). Equivalently,

\[
Q_\mu(x)
=
\int_0^\pi K_\theta(x)\,d\mu(\theta)
\]

has

\[
Q_\mu^{(n)}(0)=0,
\qquad n\ge1.
\]

In moment form,

\[
\int_0^\pi \sin(k\theta)\,\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta=0
\]

for all \(k\ge2\), while

\[
\int_0^\pi \sin\theta\,\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta>0.
\]

Thus local positive packet geometry genuinely permits source flattening.

---

# 4. Number of packet nodes needed

The moment constraints are finite-dimensional.

To match the moments

\[
\sin(k\theta),
\qquad
k=1,2,\ldots,R+3,
\]

a positive finite quadrature theorem, such as Tchakaloff/Carathéodory, gives an atomic positive measure with at most

\[
N\le R+4
\]

nodes matching all these moments exactly.

If we only match the even curvature conditions

\[
k=3,5,\ldots,2M+1,
\]

plus the value normalization, then

\[
N\le M+1
\]

or \(O(M)\) nodes suffice.

The expected jet depth is

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively

\[
R(Q)=O(\log Q).
\]

Therefore the adversary only needs

\[
\boxed{
N=O\!\left(\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}\right)
}
\]

or at worst

\[
\boxed{
N=O(\log Q)
}
\]

same-scale packets.

This is a very small finite configuration.

---

# 5. Comparison with zero-counting bounds

A local Riemann–von Mangoldt bound gives

\[
N(T+H)-N(T-H)\ll (H+1)\log T.
\]

At polynomially enlarged local scale, this is at most polynomial in \(Q\), assuming

\[
\log T\le Q^{C_T}.
\]

But the quadrature adversary needs only \(O(\log Q)\) packets. Counting estimates do not forbid such a small configuration.

Even in a narrow \(Q^{-1}\)-scale window, one generally gets at least an \(O(1)\) expected number of zeros when \(Q\sim\log T\), and on the enlarged core window one can have polynomially many available packets. Counting does not constrain their angular moment arrangement.

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Riemann--von Mangoldt counting does not rule out the anti-design.}
}
\]

It controls cardinality, not moment geometry.

---

# 6. Tests against known zero-side constraints

## 6.1 Quartet symmetry

Quartet symmetry imposes

\[
\rho,\quad \bar\rho,\quad 1-\rho,\quad 1-\bar\rho.
\]

In normalized variables, this adds reflected/symmetric packet partners. It does not destroy the quadrature mechanism.

Indeed, symmetry can automatically cancel some odd components and make the design easier. The positive continuous measure above is already symmetric with respect to the natural \(\theta\)-geometry.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{quartet symmetry does not forbid the design.}}
\]

---

## 6.2 Simplicity

Finite quadrature uses distinct nodes. It does not require multiple zeros at exactly the same location. Therefore simplicity of zeros is compatible with the adversary.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{simplicity does not forbid the design.}}
\]

---

## 6.3 Zero-density estimates

Zero-density estimates bound how many zeros can lie off the critical line in large regions. They do not exclude a finite \(O(\log Q)\)-sized packet cluster near a hypothetical off-line zero.

To help here, one would need a **local same-scale angular density theorem** saying that actual zeros near an off-line packet cannot occupy the angular positions needed by the quadrature moments. Standard zero-density estimates are far too coarse for that.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{standard zero-density estimates do not forbid the design.}}
\]

---

## 6.4 Pair correlation / spacing

Pair correlation concerns ordinate gaps, mainly for critical-line zeros and statistically over height averages. The quadrature conditions are deterministic finite moment equations in a packet-angle space involving both ordinate displacement and denominator depth.

Even strong pair-correlation information would not by itself exclude a finite exceptional cluster.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{pair correlation is diagnostic, not proof-closing.}}
\]

---

## 6.5 Functional-equation symmetry

The functional equation supplies the quartet symmetry and gamma/background contributions. The hardened countermodels in this project already survive those local symmetries. Functional-equation symmetry alone does not impose a sign-definite obstruction on the finite moment system.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{\text{functional-equation symmetry alone is insufficient.}}
\]

---

# 7. What exact zero-side theorem is missing?

The missing theorem is a deterministic anti-design statement for actual zeta zeros.

A clean version is:

**Actual-zeta no same-scale source-flattening quadrature.**  
Let \(I_\rho\) be an admissible packet interval attached to a hypothetical off-line packet. In the relevant ordinary or singular scale \(\lambda\), write

\[
m=m_0+\lambda x,
\]

and let the nearby actual-zero packets define

\[
Q_{\near}(x)=\sum_{\nu\in\mathcal L_\lambda}w_\nu K_{\theta_\nu}(x)+Q_{\mathrm{bg}}(x).
\]

Then for some fixed \(B\),

\[
\int_X |Q_{\near}''(x)+Q_{\mathrm{bg}}''(x)|^2\,dx
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

in the normalized interval corresponding to \(I_\rho\).

A finite-jet version is:

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\partial_x^r
\left(
Q_{\near}''+Q_{\mathrm{bg}}''
\right)(x_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Equivalently, actual zeta zeros cannot satisfy the finite moment system

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\approx
-\text{background moment}_k,
\qquad
3\le k\le R(Q)+3,
\]

with polynomial accuracy on an admissible off-line packet interval.

---

# 8. Is a purely zero-side proof plausible?

A purely **local** zero-side proof is not currently plausible.

Reason: the local model explicitly admits positive quadrature with \(O(R)\) nodes, and none of the standard local zero-side constraints rule out such finite designs.

A zero-side proof would need a new theorem that is much more arithmetic than existing local geometry:

\[
\boxed{
\text{actual zeta zeros have no same-scale finite-moment design around an off-line packet.}
}
\]

This theorem would likely need to use explicit-formula compatibility with primes, or a global trace/Weil positivity input. At that point it is no longer purely local zero geometry.

So the practical verdict is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 1 should be attacked through prime/AFE fixed-coefficient rigidity or global trace input,}
}
\]

with zero-side quadrature retained as the precise obstruction model and as a diagnostic for what the arithmetic theorem must forbid.

---

# 9. Final answer

The exact zero-side moment equations are:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_j w_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
}
\]

with

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j>0.
\]

For even curvature jets only:

\[
\boxed{
\sum_j w_j\sin((2\ell+1)\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
1\le \ell\le M.
}
\]

Positive finite quadrature can satisfy these with only

\[
N=O(R)
\]

nodes.

Known zero-side constraints—counting, zero-density, pair correlation, quartet symmetry, simplicity, and the functional equation—do not rule this out at polynomial accuracy.

Thus the missing zero-side theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Actual zeta zeros cannot realize same-scale source-flattening quadrature
through }R(Q)\text{ jets on an admissible off-line packet interval.}
}
\]

Absent such a theorem, a purely zero-side proof of Gate 1 is not presently credible; the next serious route is prime/AFE fixed-coefficient nonrecurrence or a global explicit-formula/trace theorem.

## Agent 2 / B — Prime/AFE fixed-coefficient incompatibility theorem

### Assignment

I am executing the Agent 2/B prompt: attack Gate 1 from the prime/AFE side. The current prompt states that Gate 1 is now the decisive arithmetic theorem, and the prime/AFE route must rule out simultaneous off-line-zero and source-flat finite-jet recurrence for actual zeta coefficients. 

Gate 1 is:

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

Use the canonical AFE-side representation:

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

---

# 1. Combined finite system in prime phases

Let

\[
z_p=e^{-im_0\log p}.
\]

For each integer

\[
n=\prod_{p\le X}p^{\nu_p(n)},
\]

we have

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
=
\prod_{p\le X}z_p^{\nu_p(n)}.
\]

Thus \(P_2(m_0)\) and all its derivatives are fixed Laurent-polynomial or ordinary polynomial functions of the prime phase vector

\[
z(m_0)=(z_p)_{p\le X}\in \mathbb T^{\pi(X)}.
\]

The source-flat finite-jet equations are:

\[
\Delta^r \partial_m^r
\left(B_2+D_2+P_2\right)(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

Since

\[
\partial_m^rP_2(m)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\log n)^r e^{-im\log n},
\]

the equations become:

\[
\boxed{
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R(Q).
}
\]

Equivalently, in prime phases:

\[
\boxed{
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r
\prod_{p\le X}z_p^{\nu_p(n)}
\approx
\mathcal T_r(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R(Q),
}
\]

where

\[
\mathcal T_r(m_0):=
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0).
\]

The off-line packet condition is modeled as

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

On the AFE side, this has the schematic form

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{n\le X_0}
c_n(\alpha)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)
\sum_{n\le Y_0}
\tilde c_n(\alpha)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
\mathcal E_\alpha(m_0)
=0.
}
\]

In prime phases this is another finite system:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z(z(m_0),\bar z(m_0);\alpha,m_0)=0.
}
\]

So the combined bad system is:

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal Z(z,\bar z;\alpha,m_0)=0,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal S_r(z,\bar z;m_0)
=
\mathcal T_r(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R(Q).
}
\]

---

# 2. Which equations use the same coefficients?

They use the same **prime phases** but not the same **coefficient weights**.

## Off-line zero equation

The off-line condition uses AFE coefficients roughly of type

\[
n^{-1/2-\alpha}
\]

and a dual part weighted by the \(\chi\)-factor:

\[
\chi(1/2+\alpha+im_0)n^{-1/2+\alpha}.
\]

So its coefficient vector is approximately:

\[
c_n(\alpha)
\sim n^{-1/2-\alpha}W_0(n/T).
\]

## Source-curvature equations

The source-curvature jet equations use differentiated log weights:

\[
a_n(-i\log n)^r,
\]

where for \(q''_{\can}\) one expects \(a_n\) to already include something like

\[
(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\]

after canonicalization. Thus the \(r\)-th source-flat jet has weights of type

\[
(\log n)^{r+2}n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\]

up to dual/gamma normalization.

So the coefficient vectors are related, but not scalar multiples:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero equation: } n^{-1/2-\alpha},
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{source jets: }(\log n)^{r+2}n^{-1/2}.
}
\]

They live on the same phase torus

\[
m_0\mapsto (e^{-im_0\log p})_{p\le X},
\]

but probe different directions in coefficient space.

This shared phase structure is the only possible source of incompatibility.

---

# 3. Is there an evident fixed-coefficient incompatibility?

I do not see a direct one.

The strongest possible hope would be a theorem saying:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\max_{0\le r\le R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

But the off-line zero equation supplies only the vanishing of one complex AFE expression. With \(\alpha\) free, this is not enough to determine many differentiated log-moment sums.

A zero of an analytic function does impose relationships among values of \(\zeta\), but it does **not** force high log-weighted sums such as

\[
\sum a_n(\log n)^{r+2}e^{-im_0\log n}
\]

to be large. Those are closer to derivatives of logarithmic phase or explicit-formula curvature, and they can in principle be small by cancellation.

So the current state is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No algebraic incompatibility is visible between }Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\text{ and source-flat jets.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Codimension and recurrence heuristic

Let

\[
R=R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively \(R=O(\log Q)\).

The source-flat system gives approximately \(R+1\) real scalar equations:

\[
\mathcal S_r(z,\bar z;m_0)\approx\mathcal T_r(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

The off-line zero condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

is one complex equation, i.e. two real equations, but \(\alpha\) is an extra real parameter. Thus after allowing \(\alpha\) to vary, it contributes effectively only \(O(1)\), plausibly one real codimension to the \(m_0\)-phase recurrence target.

Therefore the combined codimension is still approximately:

\[
\boxed{
K\sim R+O(1).
}
\]

The phase flow

\[
m_0\mapsto (e^{-im_0\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

is high-dimensional. A tube of codimension \(K\) and radius \(Q^{-C}\) has recurrence cost heuristically

\[
Q^{CK}
=
\exp(CK\log Q).
\]

Thus:

\[
R\asymp\frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{cost}\sim
\exp\!\left(O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)\right),
\]

and

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\text{cost}\sim
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)).
\]

Both are far smaller than genuinely exponential-in-\(Q\) scales.

This supports the prior heuristic:

\[
\boxed{
\text{generic recurrence remains plausible.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Does the dual term, \(\chi\)-factor, or gamma background add coercivity?

## Gamma/background \(B_2\)

The gamma/background term is smooth and deterministic. It shifts the target:

\[
\mathcal T_r(m_0)=
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0).
\]

It does not give positivity or coercivity unless one proves a lower bound saying the prime polynomial cannot approximate this moving target.

So \(B_2\) is a target shift, not an obstruction.

## Dual term \(D_2\)

The dual AFE term uses conjugate/opposite phases and \(\chi\)-weights. It couples \(z\) and \(\bar z\), but the source-flat equations already allow both real and imaginary cancellations. I do not see sign-definiteness.

The dual term may improve rigidity because it ties two ranges together through the functional equation, but that is not yet a coercive theorem.

## \(\chi\)-factor

The \(\chi\)-factor contributes a deterministic phase and amplitude depending on \(m_0\) and \(\alpha\). It is crucial for exact zeta, but locally it again shifts coefficient weights. It does not automatically imply:

\[
|q''_{\can}|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

A theorem could exploit the \(\chi\)-factor, but it would have to show fixed-coefficient incompatibility between the main and dual sums. That is currently missing.

Verdict:

\[
\boxed{
B_2,D_2,\chi \text{ add structure but no currently visible sign/coercive obstruction.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Why standard Dirichlet-polynomial tools do not close it

Large-sieve or Montgomery–Vaughan mean-value estimates usually give average bounds such as:

\[
\int_T^{T+H}|P_2(t)|^2\,dt
\]

or correlations between Dirichlet polynomials.

But Gate 1 needs a lower bound on a short interval attached to a special center \(m_0\), excluding simultaneous approximation:

\[
P_2^{(r)}(m_0)
\approx
-(B_2+D_2)^{(r)}(m_0),
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Mean-value estimates do not forbid a fixed-coefficient Dirichlet polynomial from entering a small finite-codimension tube at exceptional points.

So the needed theorem is not a generic mean-square result. It is a **center-conditioned, fixed-coefficient, finite-jet nonrecurrence theorem**.

---

# 7. Exact missing theorem

A suitable missing theorem is:

**No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence.**  
Let \(m_0\) be the center of an admissible off-line packet, so that for some transverse parameter \(\alpha\),

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]

be the canonical fixed-coefficient AFE representation. Then there exist fixed \(B\) and \(R(Q)\asymp \log Q/\log\log Q\), or a conservative \(R(Q)=O(\log Q)\), such that

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r
\left(B_2+P_2+D_2\right)(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B},
}
\]

with \(E_2\) absorbed into the error budget.

Equivalently, in prime phases,

\[
\boxed{
\left(
\mathcal Z(z,\bar z;\alpha,m_0),
\mathcal S_0(z,\bar z;m_0),
\ldots,
\mathcal S_R(z,\bar z;m_0)
\right)
}
\]

cannot enter the joint tube

\[
\{0\}\times B(Q^{-B})^{R+1}
\]

for actual zeta coefficients at an admissible off-line center.

---

# 8. What kind of coefficient rigidity would prove it?

The theorem would need one of the following.

## 8.1 Fixed-coefficient transversality

Show that near any solution of

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the vector of log-weighted derivatives

\[
\left(
\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\]

has polynomial distance from zero because the AFE coefficient vectors are quantitatively transverse.

This would be a nontrivial arithmetic statement about the actual coefficients.

## 8.2 Prime-log nonrecurrence with center conditioning

Prove that the one-parameter flow

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

does not hit the joint off-line-zero/source-flat tube at admissible centers.

This is stronger than Kronecker-style generic recurrence; it uses actual zeta coefficients and the off-line equation.

## 8.3 Explicit-formula imbalance

Show that if the source jets are flat at an off-line center, then the explicit formula creates a prime/zero imbalance elsewhere.

This would move the proof toward a global trace theorem.

---

# 9. Final verdict

I do **not** find a direct fixed-coefficient incompatibility from the current AFE structure alone.

The off-line zero equation and the source-flat jet equations use the same prime phases, but with different log-weighted coefficient vectors. That creates the possibility of rigidity, but no sign-definite or algebraic contradiction is visible.

The dual term, \(\chi\)-factor, and gamma/background terms add important actual-zeta structure, but at this stage they appear to shift and couple the finite-jet targets rather than impose coercivity.

Therefore:

\[
\boxed{
\text{generic recurrence remains plausible absent a new fixed-coefficient theorem.}
}
\]

The exact missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence for actual zeta coefficients.}
}
\]

That theorem, not a generic Dirichlet-polynomial estimate, is the prime/AFE form of Gate 1.

## Agent 2 / B — Prime/AFE nonrecurrence via coefficient transversality

### Task

I am executing the Agent 2/B prompt: test whether Gate 1 can be proved from prime/AFE **coefficient transversality**. The shared target is still Gate 1,

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|,
\]

and the bad system is an off-line center condition plus source-flat finite jets. 

---

# 1. Prime-phase formulation

Write

\[
z_p=e^{-im_0\log p},\qquad p\le X.
\]

For

\[
n=\prod_{p\le X}p^{\nu_p(n)},
\]

we have

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
=
\prod_{p\le X}z_p^{\nu_p(n)}.
\]

Thus every AFE Dirichlet polynomial becomes a function on the prime-phase torus

\[
\mathbb T^{\pi(X)}.
\]

For the source curvature,

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m),
\]

with

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_n e^{-im\log n}.
\]

The \(r\)-th normalized source-flat jet at \(m_0\) is

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^r P_2(m_0)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

So the source-jet coefficient vector is

\[
v_r(n)
=
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r.
\]

The source-flat equations are

\[
\Re\sum_{n\le X}v_r(n)e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

The off-line zero condition has AFE shape

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_{n\le X_0}b_n(\alpha)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)
\sum_{n\le Y_0}\widetilde b_n(\alpha)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
\mathcal E_\alpha(m_0)
=
0.
\]

Its coefficient vector is roughly

\[
z_\alpha(n)\sim n^{-1/2-\alpha}W_0(n/T)
\]

plus the dual vector

\[
\widetilde z_\alpha(n)\sim \chi_\alpha(m_0)n^{-1/2+\alpha}\widetilde W_0(n/T).
\]

Thus the bad system is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2+P_2)(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

---

# 2. Coefficient-vector comparison

The source-jet coefficient vectors have the schematic form

\[
v_r(n)
\sim
(\log n)^{r+2}n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\]

up to phase, dual, and smoothing conventions.

The zero-equation vector has the form

\[
z_\alpha(n)
\sim
n^{-1/2-\alpha}W_0(n/T)
\]

plus its dual.

These vectors are not scalar multiples. The log weights

\[
(\log n)^r
\]

make

\[
v_0,v_1,\ldots,v_R
\]

linearly independent in any sufficiently rich \(n\)-range. The zero-equation vector adds another independent direction unless the smoothing and support are pathologically degenerate.

So there is **formal transversality**:

\[
\boxed{
z_\alpha,\ v_0,\ldots,v_R
\text{ are generically linearly independent coefficient vectors.}
}
\]

But this is not yet an incompatibility. It only says the bad system has codimension about

\[
R+O(1).
\]

Since the prime-phase torus has dimension

\[
\pi(X),
\]

and typically

\[
\pi(X)\gg R,
\]

generic transversality predicts a high-dimensional solution set in the phase-relaxed model, not emptiness.

---

# 3. Phase-relaxed model

Relax the one-parameter condition

\[
z_p=e^{-im_0\log p}
\]

and allow

\[
z_p\in S^1
\]

independently.

The functions

\[
Z_\alpha(z),\quad \mathcal S_0(z),\ldots,\mathcal S_R(z)
\]

are trigonometric polynomials on

\[
\mathbb T^{\pi(X)}.
\]

The number of real variables is approximately

\[
\pi(X)+1
\]

including the transverse parameter \(\alpha\).

The constraints are:

\[
Z_\alpha=0
\]

which is two real equations, minus one free \(\alpha\), so effectively \(O(1)\), plus

\[
R+1
\]

real source-flat equations.

Thus the relaxed expected dimension is roughly

\[
\pi(X)-R-O(1).
\]

For any AFE length with many primes, this is positive by a huge margin.

Therefore, in the phase-relaxed model, coefficient transversality does **not** rule out the bad system. It predicts many solutions.

---

# 4. Does log-weighting create incompatibility?

The log weights make the source jets distinct:

\[
v_r(n)=a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r.
\]

But distinct coefficient vectors do not prevent simultaneous cancellation. They only make the target tube higher codimension.

A useful analogy: with many phases \(\phi_n\), one can often solve

\[
\sum_n c_{r,n}e^{i\phi_n}=t_r,
\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

provided the coefficient vectors span enough directions and there are many more phases than constraints.

The same issue appears here. Log-weighting creates a Vandermonde-like family in \(\log n\), but because the phase variables are abundant, this is a source of transversality, not contradiction.

To turn this into a lower bound, one would need a theorem saying that the **actual one-parameter orbit**

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

cannot approach the relaxed solution set at off-line centers. That is a nonrecurrence theorem, not a coefficient-linear-algebra fact.

---

# 5. Dual term and \(\chi\)-factor

The dual term \(D_2\) and the \(\chi\)-factor do add actual-zeta structure.

They couple positive and negative phase directions:

\[
e^{-im\log n}
\quad\text{and}\quad
e^{+im\log n},
\]

with deterministic gamma-dependent coefficients.

But in the finite-dimensional phase picture, they still produce additional trigonometric-polynomial terms. They do not introduce an obvious sign-definite obstruction.

They may improve transversality by adding independent coefficient directions, but that again increases codimension; it does not prove emptiness.

So the current conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
D_2,\ \chi,\ B_2
\text{ shift and couple the target, but do not visibly create coercivity.}
}
\]

A proof could exploit them, but it would need a new theorem showing that the coupled main/dual coefficient system avoids the source-flat tube.

---

# 6. Candidate transversality theorem

The strongest plausible theorem in this direction would be:

**Fixed-coefficient off-line/source transversality theorem.**  
For every admissible off-line packet center \(m_0\) and transverse parameter \(\alpha\) satisfying

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0,
\]

the coefficient vectors in the AFE representation satisfy a quantitative transversality estimate:

\[
\operatorname{dist}
\left(
0,
\left\{
\left(
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right)_{0\le r\le R}
\right\}
\right)
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

In prime-phase language, the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

does not intersect the joint tube

\[
\left\{
Z_\alpha=0,\quad
\mathcal S_0=\cdots=\mathcal S_R=0
\right\}_{Q^{-B}}.
\]

This is not ordinary linear transversality. It is an arithmetic nonrecurrence theorem for the actual zeta coefficient system.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed countermodel

A phase-relaxed countermodel is easy at the level of dimensions.

Let \(P\) be a set of primes with

\[
N=\#P\gg R.
\]

Consider simplified coefficients

\[
\mathcal S_r(z)=\Re\sum_{p\in P}c_p(\log p)^r z_p,
\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

and one zero-equation model

\[
\mathcal Z(z,\alpha)=\sum_{p\in P}d_p(\alpha)z_p.
\]

The map

\[
\Phi:\mathbb T^N\times\mathbb R_\alpha\to \mathbb R^{R+O(1)}
\]

given by

\[
(z,\alpha)\mapsto
(\mathcal Z,\mathcal S_0,\ldots,\mathcal S_R)
\]

has many more variables than equations. For generic coefficients, its Jacobian has full rank at many points, so the zero set is a manifold of dimension

\[
N-R-O(1).
\]

This demonstrates that coefficient-vector independence alone cannot imply incompatibility. One must use the actual one-parameter embedding of the phases and actual recurrence restrictions.

---

# 8. Verdict

I do **not** see a coefficient-transversality proof of Gate 1 from the current AFE structure alone.

What we have is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient vectors are generically independent/transverse}
}
\]

but:

\[
\boxed{
\text{generic transversality gives codimension, not impossibility.}
}
\]

The phase-relaxed model should have many solutions. The real problem is whether the one-parameter actual prime-log flow hits those solutions at admissible off-line centers.

Thus the missing theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence
for actual zeta coefficients.}
}
\]

Coefficient transversality may be one ingredient in such a theorem, but by itself it is not enough.

## Agent 2 / B — Prime/AFE fixed-coefficient transversality

### Task

I am executing the Agent 2/B prompt: attack Gate 1 from the prime/AFE side by checking whether the off-line zero equation and source-flat jet equations are quantitatively incompatible as fixed-coefficient phase equations. The current shared premise is that Gate 1 is the decisive bottleneck. 

Gate 1 is

\[
\int_{I_\rho}|q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\ge Q^{-B}|I_\rho|.
\]

A Gate 1 failure on

\[
I_\rho=[m_0-\Delta,m_0+\Delta],
\qquad
\Delta\asymp Q^{-1},
\]

requires

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2+P_2)(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

The center also satisfies

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

---

# 1. Prime-phase formulation

Let

\[
z_p=e^{-im_0\log p}.
\]

For each

\[
n=\prod_{p\le X}p^{\nu_p(n)},
\]

we have

\[
e^{-im_0\log n}
=
\prod_{p\le X}z_p^{\nu_p(n)}.
\]

Thus the AFE side is a trigonometric-polynomial system on the prime-phase torus

\[
\mathbb T^{\pi(X)}.
\]

Write

\[
P_2(m)=\Re\sum_{n\le X}a_ne^{-im\log n}.
\]

Then

\[
\Delta^r\partial_m^rP_2(m_0)
=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r e^{-im_0\log n}.
\]

So the source-jet coefficient vector is

\[
v_r(n)
=
a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r.
\]

The source-flat equations are

\[
\Re\sum_{n\le X}v_r(n)e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0),
\qquad
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

The off-line zero equation has the schematic AFE form

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)
=
\sum_{n\le X_0}b_n(\alpha)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)
\sum_{n\le Y_0}\widetilde b_n(\alpha)e^{+im_0\log n}
+
E_\alpha(m_0)
=
0.
\]

Thus the bad system is

\[
Z_\alpha(z,\bar z;m_0)=0,
\]

and

\[
S_r(z,\bar z;m_0):=
\Re\sum_{n\le X}v_r(n)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0)
\approx0
\]

for

\[
0\le r\le R(Q).
\]

---

# 2. Coefficient-vector comparison

The off-line zero equation uses AFE coefficient vectors of approximate type

\[
b_n(\alpha)\sim n^{-1/2-\alpha}W_0(n/T),
\]

and, through the dual term,

\[
\widetilde b_n(\alpha)\sim n^{-1/2+\alpha}\widetilde W_0(n/T).
\]

The source jets use

\[
v_r(n)=a_n(-i\Delta\log n)^r.
\]

For the curvature object \(q''_{\can}\), \(a_n\) should already contain the differentiated source-curvature weights, schematically like

\[
a_n\sim (\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/T),
\]

so

\[
v_r(n)
\sim
(\Delta\log n)^r(\log n)^2n^{-1/2}W(n/T).
\]

Therefore the coefficient vectors are:

\[
\boxed{
\text{zero equation: } n^{-1/2-\alpha}W_0(n/T)
\text{ plus dual;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{source jet }r:\ (\log n)^{r+2}n^{-1/2}W(n/T)
\text{ plus dual/background shifts.}
}
\]

They are not scalar multiples. The source jets form a log-moment family; the zero equation is a different AFE functional.

This gives **linear independence**, but not yet **incompatibility**.

---

# 3. What transversality gives

On any \(n\)-range containing many distinct values of \(\log n\), the vectors

\[
v_0,v_1,\ldots,v_R
\]

are generically independent because of the Vandermonde-like log weights

\[
1,\log n,(\log n)^2,\ldots,(\log n)^R.
\]

Adding the zero-equation vector \(b(\alpha)\) gives one or two more independent directions, unless the smoothing is pathologically degenerate.

So a plausible linear-algebra statement is:

\[
\operatorname{rank}\{b(\alpha),v_0,\ldots,v_R\}=R+O(1).
\]

But this is only a codimension statement. In the phase-relaxed model, the number of available phase variables is approximately

\[
\pi(X),
\]

which is much larger than \(R\). Thus coefficient transversality predicts a high-codimension target, not an empty target.

Concretely, if

\[
\pi(X)\gg R,
\]

then a system of \(R+O(1)\) real equations on

\[
\mathbb T^{\pi(X)}
\]

should have many phase-relaxed solutions.

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{coefficient transversality is real, but it does not prove Gate 1.}
}
\]

It only identifies the finite-codimension tube that the actual prime-log flow must avoid.

---

# 4. Does log-weighting prevent simultaneous cancellation?

Not by itself.

The source-flat equations are essentially log-moment cancellations:

\[
\sum_{n\le X}a_n(\log n)^{r+2}e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx \text{target}_r,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

The zero equation is another log-frequency sum:

\[
\sum_{n\le X_0}b_n(\alpha)e^{-im_0\log n}
+
\chi_\alpha(m_0)\sum_{n\le Y_0}\widetilde b_n(\alpha)e^{+im_0\log n}
\approx0.
\]

The fact that the weights differ by powers of \(\log n\) makes the equations independent. But because there are many phase degrees of freedom, independence is not enough. It just raises the codimension by \(R\).

A genuine proof would need to exploit the one-parameter nature of the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X},
\]

not merely the linear independence of coefficient vectors.

---

# 5. Role of \(D_2\), \(\chi\), and gamma/background terms

## Gamma/background \(B_2\)

The gamma/background term is deterministic. In the source-flat equations it shifts the target:

\[
\Re\sum v_r(n)e^{-im_0\log n}
\approx
-\Delta^r\partial_m^r(B_2+D_2)(m_0).
\]

It does not create an obvious sign or positivity obstruction.

## Dual term \(D_2\)

The dual term introduces conjugate/opposite phases and different smooth weights. It increases actual-zeta structure, but still behaves as an additional trigonometric-polynomial component.

It may improve transversality, but again transversality alone gives codimension, not exclusion.

## \(\chi\)-factor

The \(\chi\)-factor couples the main and dual sums through a deterministic amplitude and phase. It is essential for exact zeta, but I do not see a direct coercive implication of the form

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\max_{r\le R}|\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

So the conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
D_2,\ \chi,\ B_2 \text{ add structure and shift targets, but do not currently yield coercivity.}
}
\]

---

# 6. Candidate theorem if transversality can be upgraded

The best possible theorem in this direction is not ordinary coefficient transversality. It is orbit-conditional transversality.

A candidate statement is:

**Off-line-center fixed-coefficient source-jet transversality.**  
Let \(m_0\) and \(\alpha\) satisfy the admissible off-line packet equation

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Then, for

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or conservatively \(R(Q)=O(\log Q)\),

\[
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

In prime-phase terms, the actual orbit

\[
m\mapsto (e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}
\]

does not enter the joint tube

\[
Z_\alpha=0,
\qquad
S_0=\cdots=S_R=0
\]

to polynomial accuracy.

This theorem would prove the finite-jet form of Gate 1, but it is much stronger than linear coefficient independence.

---

# 7. Phase-relaxed counterexample model

A phase-relaxed model shows why coefficient transversality alone is insufficient.

Let \(N=\#P\) primes, with

\[
N\gg R.
\]

Consider simplified equations

\[
S_r(z)=\Re\sum_{p\in P}c_p(\log p)^r z_p=0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R,
\]

and

\[
Z_\alpha(z)=\sum_{p\in P}d_p(\alpha)z_p=0.
\]

The map

\[
\Phi:\mathbb T^N\times\mathbb R_\alpha
\to \mathbb R^{R+O(1)}
\]

given by

\[
(z,\alpha)\mapsto (Z_\alpha,S_0,\ldots,S_R)
\]

has many more variables than equations. For generic coefficients, the Jacobian has full rank somewhere, and the zero set has dimension

\[
N-R-O(1)>0.
\]

Thus in the phase-relaxed model, the bad system is not only possible; it is expected.

This means any successful proof must use the arithmetic rigidity of the one-parameter prime-log flow, not just the coefficient vectors.

---

# 8. Recurrence remains plausible

The joint bad system has codimension roughly

\[
K\sim R+O(1).
\]

A polynomial-accuracy target tube of radius \(Q^{-C}\) has heuristic recurrence cost

\[
Q^{CK}.
\]

If

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then

\[
Q^{CK}
=
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

If

\[
R=O(\log Q),
\]

then

\[
Q^{CK}
=
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)).
\]

Neither heuristic cost is large enough to make recurrence obviously impossible on zeta height scales. Therefore generic recurrence remains plausible unless actual coefficients impose a stronger arithmetic obstruction.

---

# 9. Final verdict

I do not find a proof of Gate 1 from coefficient transversality alone.

The correct conclusion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The coefficient vectors are transverse, but transversality only gives codimension.}
}
\]

It does not yield incompatibility because the prime-phase torus has many more degrees of freedom than the source-flat jet system imposes.

The dual term, \(\chi\)-factor, and gamma/background contributions may improve the structure of the system, but no sign-definite or coercive obstruction is visible from them alone.

So the missing theorem remains:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat finite-jet recurrence
for the actual one-parameter zeta prime-phase flow.}
}
\]

This is the prime/AFE form of Gate 1.

## Agent 2 / B — One-parameter prime-log nonrecurrence

### Task

I am executing Agent 2/B: attack the actual one-parameter recurrence problem, not the phase-relaxed model. The current shared state is that Gate 1 is central and no credible bypass is available; the relevant bad system is \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\) plus finite-jet source flatness for \(B_2+D_2+P_2\). 

---

# 1. Prime-log orbit formulation

The actual orbit is

\[
m\longmapsto z(m):=(e^{-im\log p})_{p\le X}\in \mathbb T^{\pi(X)}.
\]

The phase-relaxed model allowed arbitrary \(z_p\in S^1\), but actual zeta only samples the one-dimensional Kronecker flow generated by

\[
\omega=(\log p)_{p\le X}.
\]

The bad tube is

\[
\mathcal T_{\bad}
=
\left\{
Z_\alpha(z,m)=0,\quad
S_0(z,m)=\cdots=S_R(z,m)=0
\right\}_{Q^{-C}},
\]

where

\[
S_r(m)=
\Delta^r\partial_m^r
(B_2+D_2+P_2)(m).
\]

The desired theorem is:

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\quad\Longrightarrow\quad
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
|S_r(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}.
\]

Equivalently, the actual orbit should not hit \(\mathcal T_{\bad}\) at admissible off-line packet centers.

---

# 2. Recurrence scale for the actual orbit

The logs of distinct primes are rationally independent over \(\mathbb Q\):

\[
\sum_{p\le X} k_p\log p=0,\quad k_p\in\mathbb Z
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
\prod_{p\le X}p^{k_p}=1
\quad\Rightarrow\quad
k_p=0.
\]

So the orbit is dense in the finite torus.

The usual Kronecker heuristic says that a tube of codimension

\[
K\sim R+O(1)
\]

and radius

\[
\varepsilon=Q^{-C}
\]

should be hit on a time scale roughly

\[
\varepsilon^{-K}
=
Q^{CK}.
\]

For

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

this is

\[
\exp\!\left(
O\!\left(\frac{(\log Q)^2}{\log\log Q}\right)
\right).
\]

For the conservative

\[
R(Q)=O(\log Q),
\]

this is

\[
\exp(O((\log Q)^2)).
\]

These recurrence costs are large but not absurd on analytic number theory scales. They do not produce a contradiction by themselves.

---

# 3. Do Diophantine properties of \(\log p\) help?

There is a basic lower bound for integer relations:

\[
\left|\sum_{p\le X}k_p\log p\right|
=
\left|\log\prod_{p\le X}p^{k_p}\right|.
\]

If the product is not \(1\), then it is a rational number \(A/B\neq1\), so

\[
\left|\log(A/B)\right|
\gg \frac1{\max(A,B)}
\]

in crude terms. Since

\[
A,B\le \prod_{p\le X}p^{|k_p|},
\]

one gets

\[
\left|\sum k_p\log p\right|
\gg
\exp\!\left(-C\sum |k_p|\log p\right).
\]

This is an exponential Diophantine lower bound in coefficient height. It is far too weak to rule out polynomial-accuracy recurrence to a codimension-\(R\) tube.

To beat the volume heuristic, one would need a much stronger quantitative nonrecurrence theorem for the specific target set, not just rational independence of \(\log p\).

So:

\[
\boxed{
\text{known Diophantine facts about }\log p\text{ do not rule out the bad recurrence.}
}
\]

---

# 4. Does the off-line zero equation restrict the orbit enough?

The off-line condition

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

is one complex equation, but \(\alpha\) is a free transverse parameter. Thus it effectively imposes only \(O(1)\) additional real codimension on the prime-phase target.

It does not freeze the phase vector. It merely selects a codimension-\(O(1)\) slice of the same orbit.

The source-flat conditions add

\[
R+1
\]

real conditions:

\[
S_r(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

Thus the total bad event is still approximately codimension

\[
K=R+O(1).
\]

I do not see a mechanism by which

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\]

forces the source jets to be transverse in \(m\). It may shift the target; it does not obviously remove it.

---

# 5. Attempted one-parameter argument

A possible approach would be to consider the scalar analytic function

\[
\Psi(m,\alpha)
=
\left(
Z_\alpha(m),
S_0(m),
\ldots,S_R(m)
\right)
\]

and prove that it has no approximate zeros.

But this is a vector-valued almost-periodic function with many frequencies \(\log n\). Generic almost-periodic functions of one variable can hit small neighborhoods of high-codimension targets if the frequency vector has enough independent components and the time interval is long enough.

The only way to prove nonrecurrence would be to exploit very special structure of the coefficients:

\[
a_n,\quad b_n(\alpha),\quad \widetilde b_n(\alpha),
\quad \chi_\alpha,\quad B_2,\quad D_2.
\]

Generic finite-dimensional transversality does not suffice.

---

# 6. Candidate nonrecurrence theorem

The missing theorem must be stated directly over the one-parameter orbit.

A clean form is:

**Off-line-center source-jet nonrecurrence theorem.**  
Let \(m_0\) be the center of an admissible hypothetical off-line packet, and suppose for some \(\alpha\),

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0.
\]

Let

\[
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+P_2(m)+D_2(m)+E_2(m)
\]

be the canonical AFE representation with fixed actual-zeta coefficients. Then there exist fixed \(B\) and

\[
R(Q)\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q}
\]

or \(R(Q)=O(\log Q)\), such that

\[
\boxed{
\max_{0\le r\le R(Q)}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)
\right|
\ge Q^{-B}.
}
\]

Equivalently, the actual prime-log orbit does not enter the polynomial tube

\[
\left\{
Z_\alpha=0,\quad S_0=\cdots=S_R=0
\right\}_{Q^{-B}}.
\]

---

# 7. Is this theorem likely accessible from standard tools?

Not from standard large-sieve or mean-value estimates alone.

Those tools bound averages like

\[
\int_T^{T+H}|P(t)|^2\,dt
\]

or correlations over long intervals. They do not usually forbid exceptional approximate zeros of a vector-valued almost-periodic function at a specially conditioned center.

A more relevant tool would be a quantitative recurrence-avoidance theorem for the actual coefficient system, perhaps using:

\[
\text{explicit formula constraints},
\]

\[
\text{AFE main/dual incompatibility},
\]

\[
\text{zero-prime compatibility},
\]

or

\[
\text{global trace positivity}.
\]

But no such theorem is currently available in the draft architecture.

---

# 8. Possible ways to strengthen the attack

## 8.1 Add derivative in \(\alpha\)

If \(Z_\alpha(m_0)=0\), one can ask whether source flatness plus the zero equation forces abnormal smallness of

\[
\partial_\alpha Z_\alpha(m_0),
\quad
\partial_m Z_\alpha(m_0),
\]

or other mixed derivatives. If so, one might get a multiple-zero or near-multiple-zero contradiction.

But this requires a relation between \(q''_{\can}\) and the \(m\)-derivatives of \(Z_\alpha\). Such a relation is not yet established.

## 8.2 Use zero simplicity

If the joint bad system implied

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)\approx0,
\qquad
\partial_m Z_\alpha(m_0)\approx0,
\]

then simplicity or zero repulsion might help. But source-flatness of \(q''_{\can}\) does not obviously imply \(\partial_m Z_\alpha\approx0\). It controls phase curvature, not necessarily the AFE value derivative at the zero.

## 8.3 Enlarge the jet vector

One could include not only \(q''_{\can}\) jets, but also value/phase jets tied directly to \(Z_\alpha\). That may create a more overdetermined system. But it changes Gate 1 into a stronger theorem and must still be justified by the rank-two architecture.

---

# 9. Verdict

I cannot prove the desired implication

\[
Z_\alpha(m_0)=0
\Rightarrow
\max_{0\le r\le R}
|\Delta^r\partial_m^r q''_{\can}(m_0)|
\ge Q^{-B}
\]

from current one-parameter orbit facts.

The rational independence of \(\log p\) gives density, not avoidance. Quantitative Diophantine lower bounds for \(\log p\) are too weak to beat the volume heuristic. The off-line zero equation adds only \(O(1)\) codimension because \(\alpha\) is free.

Thus:

\[
\boxed{
\text{one-parameter recurrence remains plausible absent new actual-zeta rigidity.}
}
\]

The precise missing theorem is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No simultaneous off-line-zero/source-flat recurrence for the actual prime-log orbit.}
}
\]

This is now the prime/AFE form of Gate 1.

## Agent 2 / B — Quadrature negative-control construction

### Task

Construct the same-scale quadrature negative control for Gate 1. The purpose is to build a synthetic packet configuration where

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |q''_{\can}(m)|^2\,dm
\]

collapses, so the numerical pipeline can detect the known same-scale source-flattening adversary. This is now a numerical priority because Gate 1 is the central bottleneck and the next empirical target is same-scale finite-jet source flattening. 

---

# 1. Normalized packet kernel

Use the normalized same-scale kernel

\[
K_\theta(x)
=
\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta},
\qquad 0<\theta<\pi.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
K_\theta(x)=\Im\frac{1}{x-e^{i\theta}}.
\]

Since

\[
\frac{d^n}{dx^n}\frac{1}{x-z}
=
(-1)^n n!(x-z)^{-n-1},
\]

we get, at \(x=0\),

\[
\frac{d^n}{dx^n}\frac{1}{x-e^{i\theta}}\bigg|_{x=0}
=
-n!e^{-i(n+1)\theta}.
\]

Taking imaginary parts gives

\[
\boxed{
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta).
}
\]

Therefore, for a finite packet aggregate

\[
Q(x)=\sum_{j=1}^N w_jK_{\theta_j}(x),
\qquad w_j>0,
\]

we have

\[
Q^{(n)}(0)
=
n!\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin((n+1)\theta_j).
\]

Source-curvature flatness through order \(R\) means

\[
Q''(0)=Q^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Q^{(R+2)}(0)=0.
\]

Equivalently,

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3.
}
\]

For a cleaner centered negative control, also impose

\[
Q'(0)=0,
\]

i.e.

\[
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin(2\theta_j)=0.
\]

Keep the value positive:

\[
Q(0)=\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j>0.
\]

A convenient normalization is

\[
\boxed{
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j=1.
}
\]

---

# 2. Continuous positive quadrature source

The continuous positive measure

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta
\]

has moments

\[
\int_0^\pi \sin(k\theta)\,d\mu(\theta)
=
\frac{2}{\pi}
\int_0^\pi \sin(k\theta)\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]

By sine orthogonality,

\[
\int_0^\pi \sin(k\theta)\sin\theta\,d\theta
=
\begin{cases}
\frac{\pi}{2}, & k=1,\\
0, & k\ge2.
\end{cases}
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
\int_0^\pi \sin\theta\,d\mu(\theta)=1,
\qquad
\int_0^\pi \sin(k\theta)\,d\mu(\theta)=0\quad(k\ge2).
}
\]

The continuous aggregate

\[
Q_\mu(x)=\int_0^\pi K_\theta(x)\,d\mu(\theta)
\]

therefore satisfies

\[
Q_\mu(0)=1,
\qquad
Q_\mu^{(n)}(0)=0
\quad(n\ge1).
\]

In fact, this is the ideal source-flat control: locally it behaves as a constant profile, so

\[
Q_\mu''(x)\approx0
\]

near \(x=0\), and in the ideal model exactly constant in the appropriate local domain.

---

# 3. Finite positive quadrature construction

We need a finite positive measure

\[
\mu_N=\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\delta_{\theta_j},
\qquad w_j>0,
\]

that matches

\[
\int \sin(k\theta)\,d\mu_N(\theta)
=
\int \sin(k\theta)\,d\mu(\theta)
\]

for

\[
1\le k\le K,
\]

where

\[
K=R+3.
\]

So the constraints are

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin\theta_j=1,
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
\sum_{j=1}^N w_j\sin(k\theta_j)=0,
\qquad
2\le k\le K.
}
\]

By finite quadrature/Tchakaloff-type arguments, a positive atomic quadrature exists with

\[
N\le K+1
\]

nodes in principle. Numerically, it is often easier and more stable to use a moderately oversampled grid and solve a nonnegative least-squares or linear-programming problem.

---

# 4. Concrete numerical construction

## Option A — Positive least-squares on a dense grid

Choose a dense grid

\[
\theta_j=\frac{j\pi}{N+1},
\qquad
1\le j\le N,
\]

with

\[
N\gg K.
\]

Build the moment matrix

\[
A_{k,j}=\sin(k\theta_j),
\qquad
1\le k\le K.
\]

Set the target vector

\[
b=(1,0,0,\ldots,0)^T.
\]

Solve

\[
Aw\approx b,
\qquad
w_j\ge0,
\]

minimizing

\[
\|Aw-b\|_2.
\]

This gives a positive discrete quadrature. If exact positivity is difficult, allow a tiny tolerance and increase \(N\).

Diagnostic moment residual:

\[
\epsilon_{\mom}
=
\max_{1\le k\le K}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)-b_k
\right|.
\]

For a good negative control, require

\[
\epsilon_{\mom}\ll Q^{-B_{\test}}
\]

or simply near machine precision.

## Option B — Direct discretization of \(d\mu\)

Use quadrature for the measure

\[
d\mu(\theta)=\frac{2}{\pi}\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]

For example, choose Gauss-Legendre nodes \(y_j\in[-1,1]\), convert

\[
\theta_j=\arccos y_j,
\]

and assign weights approximating

\[
\frac{2}{\pi}\,dy
\]

under \(y=\cos\theta\), since

\[
dy=-\sin\theta\,d\theta.
\]

This gives a high-accuracy positive quadrature for the continuous moments. It may not match the trigonometric moments exactly, but with enough nodes it makes the residual very small.

## Option C — Sparse positive quadrature by linear programming

Solve:

\[
Aw=b,\qquad w\ge0,
\]

on a large grid, minimizing

\[
\|w\|_1
\]

or simply finding any feasible solution. This tends to produce a sparse quadrature with \(O(K)\) active nodes.

---

# 5. Physical rescaling

Once the normalized profile is

\[
Q(x)=\sum_jw_jK_{\theta_j}(x),
\]

choose a physical center \(m_0\) and scale \(\lambda\). Use

\[
m=m_0+\lambda x.
\]

The physical packet contribution is

\[
q_{\synthetic}(m)
=
\lambda^{-1}Q\!\left(\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda}\right).
\]

Then

\[
q_{\synthetic}''(m)
=
\lambda^{-3}Q''\!\left(\frac{m-m_0}{\lambda}\right).
\]

For a physical interval

\[
I=[m_0-\lambda X_0,\ m_0+\lambda X_0],
\]

we have

\[
E_I
=
|I|^{-1}
\int_I |q_{\synthetic}''(m)|^2\,dm.
\]

Changing variables gives

\[
E_I
=
\lambda^{-6}
(2X_0)^{-1}
\int_{-X_0}^{X_0}|Q''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

Equivalently, for the normalized Gate 1 object

\[
F_\lambda(x)=\lambda^3q_{\synthetic}''(m_0+\lambda x)=Q''(x),
\]

the negative-control energy is

\[
E_X^{\norm}
=
(2X_0)^{-1}\int_{-X_0}^{X_0}|F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
=
(2X_0)^{-1}\int_{-X_0}^{X_0}|Q''(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

This should be very small.

---

# 6. Expected finite-jet behavior

If moments are matched through

\[
1\le k\le K=R+3,
\]

then

\[
Q^{(n)}(0)=0
\qquad
1\le n\le R+2.
\]

Therefore

\[
Q''(0)=0,
\qquad
(Q'')'(0)=Q^{(3)}(0)=0,
\]

and in general

\[
(Q'')^{(r)}(0)=Q^{(r+2)}(0)=0
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

Thus the finite-jet diagnostics

\[
J_r:=
\partial_x^rF_\lambda(0)
=
Q^{(r+2)}(0)
\]

satisfy

\[
\boxed{
J_r\approx0,
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
}
\]

With moment residual \(\epsilon_{\mom}\),

\[
|J_r|
\le
(r+2)!\,\epsilon_{\mom},
\qquad
0\le r\le R.
\]

So the expected finite-jet signature is collapse through order \(R\), with factorial amplification controlled by choosing \(\epsilon_{\mom}\) sufficiently small.

---

# 7. Expected interval energy

If the quadrature is exact through order \(R+2\), then near \(x=0\),

\[
Q''(x)
=
O(x^{R+1})
\]

assuming the next derivative is bounded. Therefore, on

\[
X=[-X_0,X_0],
\]

\[
\int_X |Q''(x)|^2\,dx
=
O(X_0^{2R+3}).
\]

The normalized energy is

\[
E_X^{\norm}
=
O(X_0^{2R+2}).
\]

Thus if \(X_0<1\) and \(R\) is moderately large, the energy collapses rapidly.

In physical variables,

\[
E_I
=
\lambda^{-6}O(X_0^{2R+2}).
\]

For comparison with Gate 1, use the normalized energy

\[
\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx
=
\int_X |Q''(x)|^2\,dx,
\]

because \(F_\lambda\) removes the scale factor.

---

# 8. Expected \(B_I^{\rm eff}\)

For the synthetic control, define

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
=
-\frac{\log E_I^{\norm}}{\log Q},
\]

where

\[
E_I^{\norm}:=(2X_0)^{-1}\int_X |F_\lambda(x)|^2\,dx.
\]

If

\[
E_I^{\norm}\sim X_0^{2R+2},
\]

then

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\sim
\frac{(2R+2)|\log X_0|}{\log Q}.
\]

If

\[
R\asymp \frac{\log Q}{\log\log Q},
\]

then

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}
\asymp
\frac{|\log X_0|}{\log\log Q}.
\]

If

\[
R=C\log Q,
\]

then

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\asymp C|\log X_0|.
\]

For a strong negative control, choose either:

\[
R=O(\log Q)
\]

or a smaller interval

\[
X_0\ll1
\]

so that \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) is visibly large.

In practice, the strongest diagnostic is not the exact value of \(B_I^{\rm eff}\), but that the synthetic control produces much smaller energy than actual-zeta scans at comparable numerical resolution.

---

# 9. Pseudocode

```python
import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import lsq_linear

def build_quadrature_negative_control(R, N_grid=400, tol=1e-12):
    """
    Build positive same-scale quadrature matching moments:
        sum w_j sin(theta_j) = 1
        sum w_j sin(k theta_j) = 0, 2 <= k <= R+3
    """
    K = R + 3
    theta = np.linspace(np.pi/(N_grid+1), N_grid*np.pi/(N_grid+1), N_grid)

    A = np.vstack([np.sin(k * theta) for k in range(1, K+1)])
    b = np.zeros(K)
    b[0] = 1.0

    # Nonnegative least squares with upper bound infinity.
    result = lsq_linear(A, b, bounds=(0, np.inf), tol=tol, max_iter=20000)
    w = result.x

    moment_residual = A @ w - b
    eps_mom = np.max(np.abs(moment_residual))

    # Remove tiny weights for cleaner packet list.
    mask = w > 1e-14
    return theta[mask], w[mask], eps_mom, moment_residual

def K_theta(x, theta):
    s = np.sin(theta)
    c = np.cos(theta)
    return s / ((x - c)**2 + s**2)

def Q_profile(x, theta, w):
    vals = np.zeros_like(np.array(x, dtype=float))
    for tj, wj in zip(theta, w):
        vals += wj * K_theta(x, tj)
    return vals

def numerical_second_derivative(f_vals, dx):
    return np.gradient(np.gradient(f_vals, dx), dx)

def compute_negative_control_energy(theta, w, X0=0.25, M=2001):
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)
    dx = x[1] - x[0]
    Q = Q_profile(x, theta, w)
    Q2 = numerical_second_derivative(Q, dx)
    E_norm = np.trapz(Q2**2, x) / (2 * X0)
    S_norm = np.max(np.abs(Q2))
    return E_norm, S_norm, x, Q, Q2

def finite_jet_moments(theta, w, R):
    """
    J_r = Q^(r+2)(0) = (r+2)! sum_j w_j sin((r+3) theta_j)
    """
    J = []
    for r in range(R+1):
        n = r + 2
        moment = np.sum(w * np.sin((n+1) * theta))
        J.append(np.math.factorial(n) * moment)
    return np.array(J)

# Example use:
R = 20
theta, w, eps, residual = build_quadrature_negative_control(R)
E_norm, S_norm, x, Q, Q2 = compute_negative_control_energy(theta, w, X0=0.25)
J = finite_jet_moments(theta, w, R)
print(len(theta), eps, E_norm, S_norm, np.max(np.abs(J)))
```

---

# 10. Table schema for results

Use this for the negative-control output:

| field | meaning |
|---|---|
| \(R\) | matched source-flat jet depth |
| \(K=R+3\) | highest sine moment matched |
| \(N_{\rm grid}\) | candidate node grid size |
| \(N_{\rm active}\) | number of nonzero packet weights |
| \(\epsilon_{\mom}\) | max moment residual |
| \(X_0\) | normalized half-width |
| \(E_X^{\norm}\) | normalized curvature energy |
| \(S_X^{\norm}\) | normalized curvature sup |
| \(\max_{r\le R}|J_r|\) | finite-jet residual |
| \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) | effective flatness exponent |
| notes | positivity, conditioning, solver status |

---

# 11. Interpretation

The negative control should show:

\[
\epsilon_{\mom}\approx0,
\]

\[
J_r\approx0
\qquad(0\le r\le R),
\]

and

\[
E_X^{\norm}\ll1.
\]

If the Gate 1 numerical pipeline cannot detect this synthetic collapse, then the pipeline is not sensitive enough.

If it detects the synthetic collapse but actual-zeta scans do not show comparable collapse, that supports Gate 1 numerically.

If actual-zeta scans exhibit the same signature:

\[
E_I\ll Q^{-B},
\qquad
J_r\approx0\quad(0\le r\le R),
\]

then the current rank-two route is in serious danger and the source-flat mechanism should be diagnosed immediately.

## Agent 2 / B — Singular packet dominance/cancellation controls

### Task

I am executing Agent 2/B: build synthetic singular/shallow packet controls to validate the claim that singular Gate 2 is harmless unless it reduces to Gate 1 source flattening. The current round is focused on executable numerical/surrogate work rather than further strategic audit. 

---

# 1. Singular scaling

Let

\[
m=\gamma+cx,\qquad c\ll1,
\]

and take same-scale packets

\[
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,\qquad c_j=cd_j,\qquad d_j\asymp1.
\]

The physical packet profile is

\[
q_j(m)=w_j\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2}.
\]

Substitute \(m=\gamma+cx\):

\[
q_j(\gamma+cx)
=
w_j\frac{cd_j}{c^2(x-a_j)^2+c^2d_j^2}
=
c^{-1}w_j\frac{d_j}{(x-a_j)^2+d_j^2}.
\]

Define

\[
K_{a,d}(x)=\frac{d}{(x-a)^2+d^2},
\]

and

\[
Q(x)=\sum_j w_jK_{a_j,d_j}(x).
\]

Then

\[
\boxed{
q(\gamma+cx)=c^{-1}Q(x).
}
\]

Derivatives scale as

\[
\partial_m=c^{-1}\partial_x.
\]

Hence

\[
\boxed{
q''(\gamma+cx)=c^{-3}Q''(x),
}
\]

and

\[
\boxed{
q^{(4)}(\gamma+cx)=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
}
\]

This verifies the singular scaling.

---

# 2. Single dominant packet

Use one packet centered at \(x=0\), scale \(d=1\), weight \(w=1\):

\[
Q(x)=K(x)=\frac{1}{1+x^2}.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
Q(0)=1,
\]

\[
Q''(0)=-2,
\]

\[
Q^{(4)}(0)=24.
\]

Thus in physical coordinates,

\[
q=c^{-1},
\qquad
u=q''=c^{-3}Q''=-2c^{-3},
\]

\[
q^{(4)}=24c^{-5}.
\]

The anisotropy factors are

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

so at \(x=0\),

\[
\Gamma_G
=
-2c^{-3}-6c^{-1}+2c^{-3}
=
-6c^{-1}.
\]

Here the leading \(c^{-3}\) terms cancel for the single normalized Lorentzian at the exact center, but the result is still large:

\[
|\Gamma_G|\asymp c^{-1}.
\]

For the second anisotropy,

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
(1-q^2)u
=
(1-c^{-2})(-2c^{-3})
=
2c^{-5}-2c^{-3},
\]

and

\[
-\frac16q^{(4)}
=
-4c^{-5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
-2c^{-5}-2c^{-3},
\]

so

\[
\boxed{
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\asymp c^{-5}.
}
\]

The Gate 2 integrand is

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

Near \(x=0\),

\[
|u|^2\asymp c^{-6},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}^2\asymp c^{-10}.
\]

Thus

\[
\boxed{
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\asymp c^{-16}.
}
\]

Integrating over a physical packet-scale interval of length \(\asymp c\),

\[
\boxed{
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\asymp c^{-15}.
}
\]

So the single-packet singular regime gives Gate 2 with overwhelming margin.

---

# 3. Random same-scale cluster

For a random same-scale cluster

\[
Q(x)=\sum_{j=1}^Nw_jK_{a_j,d_j}(x),
\qquad
a_j=O(1),\quad d_j\asymp1,\quad w_j>0,
\]

the normalized quantities are usually \(O(1)\):

\[
Q,\quad Q'',\quad Q^{(4)}=O(1),
\]

unless artificially canceled.

Then

\[
q=c^{-1}Q,\qquad
u=c^{-3}Q'',
\]

\[
\Gamma_G
=
c^{-3}\left(Q''+2Q^3\right)-6c^{-1}Q,
\]

and

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}
=
c^{-5}\left(-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}\right)+c^{-3}Q''.
\]

Generically,

\[
Q''+2Q^3\not\equiv0,
\]

and

\[
-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}\not\equiv0.
\]

So typically

\[
|\Gamma_G|\asymp c^{-3},
\]

\[
|\Gamma_{G,2}|\asymp c^{-5},
\]

and

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\asymp c^{-16}
\]

on a packet-scale subinterval.

Thus random singular clusters are also Gate-2-large.

---

# 4. Singular cancellation model

To model the dangerous case, we must construct \(Q\) so that

\[
Q''\approx0
\]

and its finite jets are small on a normalized interval. This is exactly the same-scale quadrature negative control from Gate 1, now interpreted at singular scale.

Use

\[
K_\theta(x)=\frac{\sin\theta}{(x-\cos\theta)^2+\sin^2\theta}.
\]

Build

\[
Q(x)=\sum_j w_jK_{\theta_j}(x),
\qquad w_j>0,
\]

such that

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0,
\qquad
3\le k\le R+3,
\]

while

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j=1.
\]

Since

\[
K_\theta^{(n)}(0)=n!\sin((n+1)\theta),
\]

this gives

\[
Q^{(n)}(0)\approx0,
\qquad
2\le n\le R+2.
\]

Therefore

\[
Q''(0)\approx0,
\quad
(Q'')'(0)\approx0,
\quad
\ldots,
\quad
(Q'')^{(R)}(0)\approx0.
\]

In physical coordinates,

\[
u=q''=c^{-3}Q''.
\]

If \(Q''\) is flat enough, then

\[
E_I=|I|^{-1}\int_I |u|^2\,dm
\]

collapses despite the singular scaling. In normalized form,

\[
F_c(x)=c^3u(\gamma+cx)=Q''(x),
\]

so source-flatness is controlled entirely by \(Q''\), independent of \(c\).

This confirms the core claim:

\[
\boxed{
\text{singular cancellation reduces to Gate 1 source flattening in rescaled variables.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Expected scaling table

Let \(J_c=[\gamma-cX_0,\gamma+cX_0]\), so \(|J_c|=2cX_0\).

| Model | \(u=q''\) | \(\Gamma_G\) | \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) | Gate 2 mass on \(J_c\) | Gate 1 energy \(E_I\) |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| Single packet | \(c^{-3}\) | usually \(c^{-1}\) or \(c^{-3}\) | \(c^{-5}\) | \(\asymp c^{-15}\) | \(\asymp c^{-6}\) |
| Random same-scale cluster | \(c^{-3}\) | \(c^{-3}\) | \(c^{-5}\) | \(\asymp c^{-15}\) | \(\asymp c^{-6}\) |
| Quadrature-cancelled cluster | \(c^{-3}Q''\), \(Q''\approx0\) | depends on \(Q''+2Q^3\) | depends on \(-Q^2Q''-\frac16Q^{(4)}\) | may collapse only if anisotropy also cancels | collapses by construction |
| Source-flat but anisotropy live | \(u\approx0\) | can be live | can be live | small because \(|u|^2\) factor | collapses |
| Full Gate-2 cancellation | \(Q''\approx0\) plus anisotropy cancellation | small | small | collapses | collapses |

The important point is that non-cancelled singular packets are huge; only source-flattening/cancellation is dangerous.

---

# 6. Pseudocode

```python
import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import lsq_linear

def K_ad(x, a, d):
    return d / ((x - a)**2 + d**2)

def Q_profile_ad(x, a, d, w):
    Q = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)
    for aj, dj, wj in zip(a, d, w):
        Q += wj * K_ad(x, aj, dj)
    return Q

def finite_derivatives_grid(y, dx):
    y1 = np.gradient(y, dx)
    y2 = np.gradient(y1, dx)
    y3 = np.gradient(y2, dx)
    y4 = np.gradient(y3, dx)
    return y1, y2, y3, y4

def gate2_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c):
    dx = x[1] - x[0]
    Q1, Q2, Q3, Q4 = finite_derivatives_grid(Q, dx)

    q = c**(-1) * Q
    u = c**(-3) * Q2
    q4 = c**(-5) * Q4

    Gamma_G = u - 6*q + 2*q**3
    Gamma_G2 = (1 - q**2)*u - (1/6)*q4

    integrand = u**2 * (Gamma_G**2 + Gamma_G2**2)

    # physical dm = c dx
    gate2_mass = np.trapz(integrand, x) * c

    # Gate 1 physical interval-average energy:
    # E_I = (1/(2cX0)) int |u|^2 dm = (1/(2X0)) int |u|^2 dx
    X0 = max(abs(x[0]), abs(x[-1]))
    E_gate1 = np.trapz(u**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    # normalized source energy:
    F = Q2
    E_norm = np.trapz(F**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    return {
        "q": q,
        "u": u,
        "q4": q4,
        "Gamma_G": Gamma_G,
        "Gamma_G2": Gamma_G2,
        "gate2_mass": gate2_mass,
        "E_gate1_physical": E_gate1,
        "E_gate1_normalized": E_norm,
        "sup_u": np.max(np.abs(u)),
        "sup_Gamma_G": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G)),
        "sup_Gamma_G2": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G2)),
    }

def single_packet_test(c=1e-3, X0=4.0, M=4001):
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)
    a = np.array([0.0])
    d = np.array([1.0])
    w = np.array([1.0])
    Q = Q_profile_ad(x, a, d, w)
    return x, Q, gate2_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c)

def random_cluster_test(c=1e-3, N=8, X0=4.0, M=4001, seed=0):
    rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)
    a = rng.uniform(-1.0, 1.0, size=N)
    d = rng.uniform(0.6, 1.4, size=N)
    w = rng.uniform(0.2, 1.0, size=N)
    Q = Q_profile_ad(x, a, d, w)
    return x, Q, gate2_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c), (a, d, w)

def build_quadrature_cluster(R=20, N_grid=300, tol=1e-12):
    """
    Build positive weights w_j on theta grid satisfying:
      sum w_j sin(theta_j) = 1
      sum w_j sin(k theta_j) = 0 for 2 <= k <= R+3
    Then convert theta to a=cos(theta), d=sin(theta).
    """
    Kmax = R + 3
    theta = np.linspace(np.pi/(N_grid+1), N_grid*np.pi/(N_grid+1), N_grid)

    A = np.vstack([np.sin(k * theta) for k in range(1, Kmax + 1)])
    b = np.zeros(Kmax)
    b[0] = 1.0

    res = lsq_linear(A, b, bounds=(0, np.inf), tol=tol, max_iter=20000)
    w = res.x
    mask = w > 1e-13

    theta = theta[mask]
    w = w[mask]
    a = np.cos(theta)
    d = np.sin(theta)

    moment_resid = A @ res.x - b
    eps = np.max(np.abs(moment_resid))
    return a, d, w, eps

def quadrature_cancelled_test(c=1e-3, R=20, X0=0.25, M=2001):
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)
    a, d, w, eps = build_quadrature_cluster(R=R)
    Q = Q_profile_ad(x, a, d, w)
    out = gate2_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c)
    out["moment_residual"] = eps
    out["N_active"] = len(w)
    return x, Q, out, (a, d, w)
```

---

# 7. Recommended parameter set

Use these for first validation:

| parameter | value |
|---|---:|
| \(c\) | \(10^{-2},10^{-3},10^{-4}\) |
| \(X_0\), single/random | \(4\) |
| \(X_0\), cancellation | \(0.25\) or \(0.5\) |
| grid \(M\) | \(2001\) to \(8001\) |
| random cluster \(N\) | \(8,16,32\) |
| quadrature \(R\) | \(10,20,40\) |
| quadrature \(N_{\rm grid}\) | \(300\) to \(1000\) |
| moment residual target | \(<10^{-10}\) initially |

Expected results:

1. **Single packet:**  
   \[
   E_{\rm norm}=O(1),\quad E_{\rm physical}\asymp c^{-6},\quad
   \text{Gate 2 mass}\asymp c^{-15}.
   \]

2. **Random cluster:**  
   \[
   E_{\rm norm}=O(1)\text{ or larger},\quad
   \text{Gate 2 mass huge}.
   \]

3. **Quadrature-cancelled cluster:**  
   \[
   E_{\rm norm}\ll1,
   \quad
   J_r\approx0\ (0\le r\le R),
   \]
   with \(E_{\rm norm}\) decreasing as \(R\) increases or \(X_0\) shrinks.

---

# 8. Output table schema

| run type | \(c\) | \(N\) active | \(R\) | \(X_0\) | moment residual | \(E_{\rm norm}\) | \(E_{\rm physical}\) | \(\sup|u|\) | \(\sup|\Gamma_G|\) | \(\sup|\Gamma_{G,2}|\) | Gate 2 mass |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| single |  | 1 | — |  | — |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| random |  | \(N\) | — |  | — |  |  |  |  |  |  |
| quadrature |  | active | \(R\) |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |  |

---

# 9. Interpretation

The controls should verify three things:

1. **Singular dominance:** a non-cancelled shallow packet gives enormous Gate 2 mass.

2. **Singular cancellation:** if a same-scale cluster cancels \(Q''\), Gate 1 energy collapses in normalized variables.

3. **Reduction to Gate 1:** the only dangerous singular case is the same source-flattening adversary already isolated by Gate 1.

So if actual-zeta scans later show singular-looking behavior, compare them against these controls:

\[
\boxed{
\text{single/random singular controls} \Rightarrow \text{healthy largeness;}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{quadrature control} \Rightarrow \text{dangerous source-flat signature.}
}
\]
