## Agent 2 / B — Executable singular control design

### Task

Build implementation-ready singular/shallow packet controls. The aim is to validate numerically that singular packets are harmless by dominance unless they reduce to Gate 1 source-flattening by same-scale cancellation. This follows the current execution-oriented prompt: implement controls first, then compare against actual-zero and AFE scans. 

---

# 1. Model and scaling

Use

\[
m=\gamma+cx,
\qquad c\ll 1,
\]

and packet profiles

\[
q(m)=\sum_j w_j\frac{c_j}{(m-\gamma_j)^2+c_j^2},
\qquad
\gamma_j=\gamma+ca_j,
\qquad
c_j=cd_j.
\]

Then

\[
q(\gamma+cx)
=
c^{-1}Q(x),
\]

where

\[
Q(x)=\sum_jw_jK_{a_j,d_j}(x),
\qquad
K_{a,d}(x)=\frac{d}{(x-a)^2+d^2}.
\]

Derivatives scale as

\[
q''(\gamma+cx)=c^{-3}Q''(x),
\]

\[
q^{(4)}(\gamma+cx)=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}(x).
\]

Set

\[
u=q''_{\can},
\]

\[
\Gamma_G=u-6q+2q^3,
\]

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}=(1-q^2)u-\frac16q^{(4)}.
\]

The Gate 2 integrand is

\[
|u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2).
\]

---

# 2. Expected asymptotics

## Single dominant packet

Use

\[
Q(x)=\frac{1}{1+x^2}.
\]

At \(x=0\),

\[
Q(0)=1,\qquad Q''(0)=-2,\qquad Q^{(4)}(0)=24.
\]

So

\[
q\sim c^{-1},
\qquad
u=q''\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
q^{(4)}\sim c^{-5}.
\]

The second anisotropy satisfies

\[
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5}.
\]

Therefore

\[
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

Integrated over a packet-scale interval of physical length \(\asymp c\),

\[
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm
\asymp c^{-15}.
\]

This is the dominance control.

## Random same-scale cluster

For random

\[
a_j=O(1),
\qquad d_j\asymp1,
\qquad w_j>0,
\]

typically

\[
Q,\ Q'',\ Q^{(4)}=O(1),
\]

hence again

\[
u\sim c^{-3},
\qquad
\Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},
\qquad
\text{Gate 2 mass}\sim c^{-15}.
\]

## Quadrature-cancelled cluster

Use same-scale quadrature to force

\[
Q''(0)\approx Q^{(3)}(0)\approx\cdots\approx Q^{(R+2)}(0)\approx0.
\]

Then

\[
u=c^{-3}Q''
\]

is small in normalized coordinates. In normalized form

\[
F_c(x)=c^3u(\gamma+cx)=Q''(x),
\]

so singular source collapse is exactly the Gate 1 negative-control mechanism.

---

# 3. Implementation-ready Python

```python
import numpy as np
from scipy.optimize import lsq_linear

# -----------------------------
# Kernels and numerical derivatives
# -----------------------------

def K_ad(x, a, d):
    return d / ((x - a)**2 + d**2)

def Q_profile(x, a, d, w):
    Q = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)
    for aj, dj, wj in zip(a, d, w):
        Q += wj * K_ad(x, aj, dj)
    return Q

def derivatives_1_to_4(y, dx):
    y1 = np.gradient(y, dx, edge_order=2)
    y2 = np.gradient(y1, dx, edge_order=2)
    y3 = np.gradient(y2, dx, edge_order=2)
    y4 = np.gradient(y3, dx, edge_order=2)
    return y1, y2, y3, y4

def gate_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c):
    dx = x[1] - x[0]
    Q1, Q2, Q3, Q4 = derivatives_1_to_4(Q, dx)

    q = c**(-1) * Q
    u = c**(-3) * Q2
    q4 = c**(-5) * Q4

    Gamma_G = u - 6*q + 2*q**3
    Gamma_G2 = (1 - q**2)*u - (1.0/6.0)*q4

    gate2_integrand = u**2 * (Gamma_G**2 + Gamma_G2**2)

    # Physical dm = c dx.
    gate2_mass = c * np.trapz(gate2_integrand, x)

    X0 = max(abs(x[0]), abs(x[-1]))

    # Physical interval-average Gate 1 energy:
    # E_I = 1/(2cX0) * ∫ |u|^2 dm
    #     = 1/(2X0)  * ∫ |u|^2 dx
    E_gate1_physical = np.trapz(u**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    # Normalized Gate 1 energy for F_c = c^3 u = Q''.
    E_gate1_normalized = np.trapz(Q2**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    return {
        "q": q,
        "u": u,
        "q4": q4,
        "Gamma_G": Gamma_G,
        "Gamma_G2": Gamma_G2,
        "gate2_mass": gate2_mass,
        "E_gate1_physical": E_gate1_physical,
        "E_gate1_normalized": E_gate1_normalized,
        "sup_q": np.max(np.abs(q)),
        "sup_u": np.max(np.abs(u)),
        "sup_q4": np.max(np.abs(q4)),
        "sup_Gamma_G": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G)),
        "sup_Gamma_G2": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G2)),
        "sup_gate2_integrand": np.max(np.abs(gate2_integrand)),
    }

# -----------------------------
# Control 1: single packet dominance
# -----------------------------

def single_packet_control(c=1e-3, X0=4.0, M=8001):
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)
    a = np.array([0.0])
    d = np.array([1.0])
    w = np.array([1.0])
    Q = Q_profile(x, a, d, w)
    out = gate_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c)
    return x, Q, out, (a, d, w)

# -----------------------------
# Control 2: random same-scale cluster
# -----------------------------

def random_cluster_control(c=1e-3, N=12, X0=4.0, M=8001, seed=0):
    rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)

    a = rng.uniform(-1.0, 1.0, size=N)
    d = rng.uniform(0.6, 1.4, size=N)
    w = rng.uniform(0.2, 1.0, size=N)

    Q = Q_profile(x, a, d, w)
    out = gate_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c)
    return x, Q, out, (a, d, w)

# -----------------------------
# Control 3: quadrature-cancelled singular cluster
# -----------------------------

def build_sine_quadrature(R):
    """
    Deterministic positive quadrature:
      theta_j = j*pi/(N+1), N = R+3
      w_j = 2/(N+1) sin(theta_j)

    This gives:
      sum_j w_j sin(theta_j) = 1
      sum_j w_j sin(k theta_j) = 0 for 2 <= k <= N.
    """
    N = R + 3
    j = np.arange(1, N + 1)
    theta = j * np.pi / (N + 1)
    w = (2.0 / (N + 1)) * np.sin(theta)

    a = np.cos(theta)
    d = np.sin(theta)

    return theta, a, d, w

def quadrature_cancelled_control(c=1e-3, R=24, X0=0.25, M=4001):
    x = np.linspace(-X0, X0, M)

    theta, a, d, w = build_sine_quadrature(R)
    Q = Q_profile(x, a, d, w)
    out = gate_quantities_from_Q(x, Q, c)

    # Moment checks.
    Kmax = R + 3
    moments = []
    for k in range(1, Kmax + 1):
        moments.append(np.sum(w * np.sin(k * theta)))
    moments = np.array(moments)

    out["moment_value_k1"] = moments[0]
    out["max_moment_residual_k2_to_K"] = np.max(np.abs(moments[1:]))
    out["R"] = R
    out["N_active"] = len(w)

    return x, Q, out, (a, d, w, theta)

# -----------------------------
# Scaling report
# -----------------------------

def summarize_run(label, c, out):
    return {
        "label": label,
        "c": c,
        "sup_q": out["sup_q"],
        "sup_u": out["sup_u"],
        "sup_q4": out["sup_q4"],
        "sup_Gamma_G": out["sup_Gamma_G"],
        "sup_Gamma_G2": out["sup_Gamma_G2"],
        "E_gate1_physical": out["E_gate1_physical"],
        "E_gate1_normalized": out["E_gate1_normalized"],
        "gate2_mass": out["gate2_mass"],
        "sup_gate2_integrand": out["sup_gate2_integrand"],
    }

def run_singular_controls():
    rows = []
    for c in [1e-2, 1e-3, 1e-4]:
        _, _, out1, _ = single_packet_control(c=c)
        rows.append(summarize_run("single", c, out1))

        _, _, out2, _ = random_cluster_control(c=c, seed=1)
        rows.append(summarize_run("random_cluster", c, out2))

        _, _, out3, _ = quadrature_cancelled_control(c=c, R=24, X0=0.25)
        rows.append(summarize_run("quadrature_cancelled", c, out3))

    return rows
```

---

# 4. Expected scaling table

Use the following expected orders to verify the implementation.

| Control | \(q\) | \(u=q''\) | \(q^{(4)}\) | \(\Gamma_G\) | \(\Gamma_{G,2}\) | Gate 2 mass over \(c\)-scale | Normalized Gate 1 energy |
|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| single packet | \(c^{-1}\) | \(c^{-3}\) | \(c^{-5}\) | \(c^{-1}\) at center, often \(c^{-3}\) off-center | \(c^{-5}\) | \(c^{-15}\) | \(O(1)\) |
| random cluster | \(c^{-1}\) | \(c^{-3}\) | \(c^{-5}\) | \(c^{-3}\) typically | \(c^{-5}\) typically | \(c^{-15}\) | \(O(1)\) or larger |
| quadrature-cancelled | \(c^{-1}\) | \(c^{-3}Q''\), with \(Q''\approx0\) near center | depends on matched order | may remain live unless further cancellation | may remain live unless further cancellation | only small if source and anisotropy cancel | small by construction |

For \(c=10^{-2},10^{-3},10^{-4}\), the expected single/random Gate 2 mass scales approximately as:

| \(c\) | \(c^{-15}\) |
|---:|---:|
| \(10^{-2}\) | \(10^{30}\) |
| \(10^{-3}\) | \(10^{45}\) |
| \(10^{-4}\) | \(10^{60}\) |

The exact numerical constant depends on interval width \(X_0\), finite-difference accuracy, and whether the center point cancellation in \(\Gamma_G\) is sampled, but the scaling should be unmistakable.

---

# 5. Diagnostics distinguishing dominance from cancellation

Use these diagnostics.

## Dominance signature

A singular dominance run should show:

\[
\sup|u|\asymp c^{-3},
\]

\[
\sup|\Gamma_{G,2}|\asymp c^{-5},
\]

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass}\asymp c^{-15},
\]

and

\[
E_{\rm norm}:=\frac1{|X|}\int_X |Q''|^2dx=O(1).
\]

## Random-cluster signature

Same as dominance, but with less predictable constants:

\[
E_{\rm norm}=O(1)\text{ or larger},
\]

\[
\text{Gate 2 mass huge}.
\]

## Cancellation signature

A quadrature-cancelled run should show:

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin\theta_j\approx1,
\]

\[
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\approx0
\qquad(2\le k\le R+3),
\]

\[
F_c(x)=c^3u=Q''(x)
\]

has small finite jets at \(0\):

\[
F_c^{(r)}(0)\approx0,
\qquad 0\le r\le R.
\]

The normalized Gate 1 energy

\[
E_{\rm norm}=\frac1{|X|}\int_X|Q''|^2dx
\]

should be much smaller than the single/random controls on small \(X_0\), especially as \(R\) increases.

---

# 6. Recommended parameters

Initial pilot:

\[
c\in\{10^{-2},10^{-3},10^{-4}\},
\]

\[
R\in\{12,24,40\},
\]

\[
X_0=4.0
\]

for single/random dominance tests,

\[
X_0\in\{0.25,0.5\}
\]

for quadrature-cancelled tests.

Grid size:

\[
M=4001
\]

minimum;

\[
M=8001\text{ or }16001
\]

for \(c=10^{-4}\) or high \(R\).

For high \(R\), finite differences become noisy. Prefer analytic moment checks for jets and use interval energy for \(Q''\) computed either by analytic derivatives of \(K_{a,d}\) or high-resolution numerical differentiation.

---

# 7. Pass/fail checklist

The singular-control module is working if:

1. **Single packet:**  
   \[
   \log(\text{Gate 2 mass})/\log(1/c)\approx15.
   \]

2. **Random cluster:**  
   Gate 2 mass also grows polynomially like a high power of \(1/c\), typically near \(c^{-15}\).

3. **Quadrature cluster:**  
   moment residuals satisfy

   \[
   \max_{2\le k\le R+3}
   \left|\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)\right|
   \lesssim10^{-12}
   \]

   in double precision for moderate \(R\).

4. **Quadrature cluster:**  
   normalized source energy \(E_{\rm norm}\) is much smaller on \(X_0=0.25\) than in single/random controls.

5. **Interpretation:**  
   dominance is huge; only source-flattening quadrature produces the dangerous signature.

## Agent 2 / B — Singular-control code review and scaling sanity checks

### Scope

I am executing Agent 2/B: review and harden the singular/shallow-packet control design, focusing on numerical stability, analytic derivatives, expected scaling, diagnostics, and output schema. This directly supports the Gate 1 test harness execution plan. 

---

# 1. Main numerical risk

The proposed finite-difference implementation is acceptable for a smoke test, but it is **not reliable** for the singular controls at

\[
c=10^{-4}
\]

because the quantities scale as high powers:

\[
u\sim c^{-3},\qquad \Gamma_{G,2}\sim c^{-5},\qquad
|u|^2|\Gamma_{G,2}|^2\sim c^{-16}.
\]

For \(c=10^{-4}\),

\[
c^{-16}=10^{64}.
\]

This is below double-precision overflow, but numerical differentiation error is amplified by powers of \(c^{-3}\) and \(c^{-5}\). The fourth derivative \(Q^{(4)}\) computed by repeated finite differences is the main instability.

Recommendation:

\[
\boxed{\text{Use analytic formulas for } Q'',Q^{(4)}.}
\]

Finite differences should only be used as a debugging cross-check.

---

# 2. Analytic derivative formulas

For

\[
K_{a,d}(x)=\frac{d}{(x-a)^2+d^2},
\qquad y=x-a,
\]

we have:

\[
K''_{a,d}(x)
=
\frac{2d(3y^2-d^2)}{(y^2+d^2)^3}.
\]

The fourth derivative is:

\[
K^{(4)}_{a,d}(x)
=
\frac{24d(5y^4-10d^2y^2+d^4)}{(y^2+d^2)^5}.
\]

So for

\[
Q(x)=\sum_jw_jK_{a_j,d_j}(x),
\]

use:

\[
Q''(x)=\sum_jw_jK''_{a_j,d_j}(x),
\]

\[
Q^{(4)}(x)=\sum_jw_jK^{(4)}_{a_j,d_j}(x).
\]

Then:

\[
q=c^{-1}Q,
\qquad
u=q''=c^{-3}Q'',
\qquad
q^{(4)}=c^{-5}Q^{(4)}.
\]

---

# 3. Implementation-ready functions

```python
import numpy as np

def K_ad(x, a, d):
    y = x - a
    return d / (y*y + d*d)

def K2_ad(x, a, d):
    y = x - a
    den = y*y + d*d
    return 2*d*(3*y*y - d*d) / den**3

def K4_ad(x, a, d):
    y = x - a
    den = y*y + d*d
    return 24*d*(5*y**4 - 10*d*d*y*y + d**4) / den**5

def Q_all(x, a, d, w):
    Q = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)
    Q2 = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)
    Q4 = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)

    for aj, dj, wj in zip(a, d, w):
        Q += wj * K_ad(x, aj, dj)
        Q2 += wj * K2_ad(x, aj, dj)
        Q4 += wj * K4_ad(x, aj, dj)

    return Q, Q2, Q4

def singular_gate_quantities(x, a, d, w, c):
    Q, Q2, Q4 = Q_all(x, a, d, w)

    q = c**(-1) * Q
    u = c**(-3) * Q2
    q4 = c**(-5) * Q4

    Gamma_G = u - 6*q + 2*q**3
    Gamma_G2 = (1 - q**2)*u - (1/6)*q4

    gate2_integrand = u**2 * (Gamma_G**2 + Gamma_G2**2)

    X0 = max(abs(x[0]), abs(x[-1]))

    # Physical dm = c dx.
    gate2_mass = c * np.trapz(gate2_integrand, x)

    # Physical Gate 1 interval-average energy.
    E_gate1_physical = np.trapz(u**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    # Normalized Gate 1 energy: F_c = c^3 u = Q''.
    E_gate1_normalized = np.trapz(Q2**2, x) / (2 * X0)

    return {
        "Q": Q,
        "Q2": Q2,
        "Q4": Q4,
        "q": q,
        "u": u,
        "q4": q4,
        "Gamma_G": Gamma_G,
        "Gamma_G2": Gamma_G2,
        "gate2_mass": gate2_mass,
        "E_gate1_physical": E_gate1_physical,
        "E_gate1_normalized": E_gate1_normalized,
        "sup_Q2": np.max(np.abs(Q2)),
        "sup_Q4": np.max(np.abs(Q4)),
        "sup_q": np.max(np.abs(q)),
        "sup_u": np.max(np.abs(u)),
        "sup_q4": np.max(np.abs(q4)),
        "sup_Gamma_G": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G)),
        "sup_Gamma_G2": np.max(np.abs(Gamma_G2)),
        "sup_gate2_integrand": np.max(np.abs(gate2_integrand)),
    }
```

---

# 4. Control generators

## 4.1 Single packet dominance

```python
def single_packet_params():
    a = np.array([0.0])
    d = np.array([1.0])
    w = np.array([1.0])
    return a, d, w
```

Expected:

\[
\sup |u|\asymp c^{-3},
\qquad
\sup |\Gamma_{G,2}|\asymp c^{-5},
\qquad
\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)\,dm\asymp c^{-15}.
\]

## 4.2 Random same-scale cluster

```python
def random_cluster_params(N=12, seed=1):
    rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
    a = rng.uniform(-1.0, 1.0, size=N)
    d = rng.uniform(0.6, 1.4, size=N)
    w = rng.uniform(0.2, 1.0, size=N)
    return a, d, w
```

Expected: same high-power Gate 2 dominance, with constants depending on cluster geometry.

## 4.3 Quadrature-cancelled singular cluster

Use the deterministic sine quadrature:

\[
\theta_j=\frac{j\pi}{N+1},
\qquad
w_j=\frac{2}{N+1}\sin\theta_j.
\]

Convert:

\[
a_j=\cos\theta_j,\qquad d_j=\sin\theta_j.
\]

```python
def sine_quadrature_params(R):
    N = R + 3
    j = np.arange(1, N + 1)
    theta = j * np.pi / (N + 1)
    w = (2.0 / (N + 1)) * np.sin(theta)
    a = np.cos(theta)
    d = np.sin(theta)
    return theta, a, d, w

def check_sine_moments(theta, w, R):
    Kmax = R + 3
    moments = np.array([np.sum(w * np.sin(k * theta)) for k in range(1, Kmax + 1)])
    value_error = abs(moments[0] - 1.0)
    flat_error = np.max(np.abs(moments[1:])) if Kmax >= 2 else 0.0
    return value_error, flat_error, moments
```

Expected:

\[
Q''(0)=Q^{(3)}(0)=\cdots=Q^{(R+2)}(0)=0
\]

up to floating-point error, hence the normalized source energy should be much smaller near \(x=0\) than in the single/random controls.

| quadrature cancelled | \(10^{-2},10^{-3},10^{-4}\) | \(0.25,0.5,0.75\) | 4001 | \(R=12,24,40\) |

# 7. Diagnostics

## Dominance diagnostics

A run is dominance-like if:

\[
\log(\sup|u|)/\log(1/c)\approx 3,
\]

\[
\log(\sup|\Gamma_{G,2}|)/\log(1/c)\approx 5,
\]

\[
\log(\text{Gate 2 mass})/\log(1/c)\approx 15.
\]

Use log-slope checks across \(c=10^{-2},10^{-3},10^{-4}\).

## Source-cancellation diagnostics

A run is source-cancellation-like if:

\[
E_{\rm norm}=\frac1{|X|}\int_X |Q''|^2\,dx
\]

is much smaller than the single/random controls and decreases sharply as \(R\) increases or \(X_0\) decreases.

Also require moment residual:

\[
\max_{2\le k\le R+3}
\left|
\sum_jw_j\sin(k\theta_j)
\right|
\le 10^{-10}
\]

for \(R\le 40\) in double precision.

---

# 8. False positives and bug checks

## 8.1 Overflow

For \(c=10^{-4}\), the largest expected values are around:

\[
c^{-16}=10^{64},
\]

well below double overflow \(\sim10^{308}\). Overflow should not occur unless \(c\ll10^{-10}\) or weights/geometries create near-poles with \(d_j\ll1\).

Guardrail:

\[
d_j\ge0.1
\]

for random clusters.

## 8.2 Endpoint artifacts

Large \(X_0\) can include regions close to packet centers \(a_j\), especially for quadrature nodes with \(a_j\in[-1,1]\). This is not a singularity because \(d_j>0\), but it can increase energy and mask local cancellation.

Use:

\[
X_0=0.25
\]

as the primary cancellation test.

## 8.3 Numerical derivative error

Avoid repeated finite differences. Use analytic \(Q''\) and \(Q^{(4)}\). If finite differences are used as a debug check, compare:

\[
\|Q''_{\rm finite}-Q''_{\rm analytic}\|_\infty.
\]

Reject if relative error exceeds \(10^{-6}\).

## 8.4 Moment residual hidden by factorial amplification

Jets satisfy:

\[
Q^{(n)}(0)=n!\sum_jw_j\sin((n+1)\theta_j).
\]

Even a small moment residual can be amplified by \(n!\). For \(R=40\), do not use raw factorial jet magnitudes in double precision as the main pass/fail condition. Use moment residuals and interval energy instead.

## 8.5 Cancellation from roundoff

For quadrature cancellation, exact moments may appear as \(10^{-15}\) due to floating-point sine orthogonality. That is fine for pipeline validation but not a proof-level object. If needed, recompute the moments with high precision to verify.

---

# 9. Output schema

Use this table for each run:

| field | description |
|---|---|
| `run_type` | `single`, `random`, `quadrature_cancelled` |
| `c` | singular scale |
| `X0` | normalized half-width |
| `M` | grid size |
| `R` | quadrature jet depth, if applicable |
| `N_packets` | number of packets |
| `moment_value_error` | \(|\sum w_j\sin\theta_j-1|\) |
| `moment_flat_error` | max moment residual for \(2\le k\le R+3\) |
| `E_norm` | \(|X|^{-1}\int |Q''|^2 dx\) |
| `E_physical` | physical Gate 1 energy |
| `sup_u` | \(\sup |q''|\) |
| `sup_Gamma_G` | \(\sup|\Gamma_G|\) |
| `sup_Gamma_G2` | \(\sup|\Gamma_{G,2}|\) |
| `gate2_mass` | \(\int |u|^2(\Gamma_G^2+\Gamma_{G,2}^2)dm\) |
| `log_slope_gate2` | slope across \(c\), computed after batch |
| `classification` | `dominance`, `source_cancelled`, or `bug/unstable` |

---

_Thought for 3m 18s_

Ran the **AFE/fixed-prime surrogate pilot**. This is a surrogate-only execution step, not canonical zeta evidence. It tests whether source-flat finite jets are easy to find in increasingly constrained prime-phase models, as requested in the execution plan. 

## Setup

I used a smoothed von Mangoldt / prime-power model:

\[
P_2(t)=\Re\sum_{n\le 350} a_n e^{-it\log n},
\]

with

\[
a_n\propto \Lambda(n)(\log n)^2 n^{-1/2}W(n),
\]

normalized so the \(r=0\) main term has unit-scale RMS.

For source-flatness, I minimized:

\[
\mathcal J_{\rm src}(t)
=
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_t^r q_{\rm surr}(t)
\right|^2,
\qquad
\Delta=\frac1{\log t}.
\]

For the off-line-center proxy, I used:

\[
\mathcal J(t,\alpha)
=
|Z_\alpha(t)|^2+
\sum_{r=0}^{R}
\left|
\Delta^r\partial_t^r q_{\rm surr}(t)
\right|^2.
\]

Search range:

\[
80\le t\le 4000,
\qquad
0.01\le \alpha\le0.35.
\]

## Level definitions

| level | model |
|---:|---|
| 1 | main fixed-prime / prime-power source model only |
| 2 | main + \(\chi\)-like dual term |
| 3 | main + dual + smooth background |
| 4 | Level 3 + off-line-center proxy \(Z_\alpha(t)=0\) |

## Source-flat surrogate results

The surrogate readily finds points with small source-jet vectors. The values below are normalized; \(\max|J_r|\) is the maximum normalized finite-jet component for \(0\le r\le R\).

|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 4 | 1 | 2382.711 | \(1.178\times10^{-2}\) | \(9.313\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.633\times10^{-3}\) | 3.129 |
| 4 | 2 | 2856.150 | \(2.343\times10^{-3}\) | \(3.185\times10^{-2}\) | \(8.615\times10^{-4}\) | 3.402 |
| 4 | 3 | 2382.647 | \(1.479\times10^{-3}\) | \(2.962\times10^{-2}\) | \(2.133\times10^{-6}\) | 6.367 |
| 6 | 1 | 2382.658 | \(1.785\times10^{-2}\) | \(8.062\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.301\times10^{-3}\) | 3.240 |
| 6 | 2 | 2382.643 | \(1.358\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.089\times10^{-1}\) | \(1.820\times10^{-2}\) | 1.953 |
| 6 | 3 | 2382.643 | \(1.729\times10^{-3}\) | \(3.047\times10^{-2}\) | \(2.293\times10^{-6}\) | 6.331 |

\[
E_I\sim2\times10^{-6},
\qquad
B_I^{\rm eff}\approx6.3.
\]

That is not a proof-relevant result, but it confirms the surrogate system can produce robust source-flat-looking intervals.

## Joint off-line-center proxy results

Adding the off-line-center proxy made the objective worse but did **not** eliminate small finite-jet candidates.

| \(R\) | best \(t\) | best \(\alpha\) | total \(\mathcal J\) | source part | \(|Z_\alpha|^2\) | \(\max |J_r|\) |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 4 | 1580.517 | 0.010 | \(1.491\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.396\times10^{-2}\) | \(9.476\times10^{-4}\) | \(6.854\times10^{-2}\) |
| 6 | 1517.737 | 0.010 | \(2.881\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.661\times10^{-2}\) | \(1.220\times10^{-2}\) | \(8.145\times10^{-2}\) |

The optimizer pushed \(\alpha\) to the lower bound \(0.01\), which means this proxy wants the off-line condition as close to the critical line as allowed. That is consistent with the earlier concern that \(\alpha\) is a free transverse parameter and only adds \(O(1)\) codimension.

## Interpretation

This surrogate pilot **threatens Gate 1 at the surrogate level**, but does not threaten actual zeta yet.

What it shows:

\[
\text{fixed-prime/AFE-like phase models can produce source-flat finite jets.}
\]

What it does **not** show:

\[
\text{actual }q''_{\can}\text{ has source-flat intervals.}
\]

The important operational conclusion is that Gate 1 is not protected by generic oscillation or by adding a dual/background term in this simplified model. Actual zeta must use stronger arithmetic compatibility than these surrogates encode.

## Assistant (2026-04-26 15:18:57)

_Thought for 10s_

Below is a **single Python script** for the next test: a **reoptimized cutoff/smoothing sweep** for the fixed-prime/AFE-style surrogate, with optional actual-zero-proxy cross-check near the best candidates.

Save as:

```bash
gate1_surrogate_sweep.py
```

Run basic surrogate sweep:

```bash
python gate1_surrogate_sweep.py
```

Run with actual-zero proxy cross-checks for best candidates:

```bash
python gate1_surrogate_sweep.py --actual-zero-proxy
```

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Gate 1 surrogate reoptimization sweep.

Purpose:
  For each cutoff/smoothing model, re-optimize the source-flat objective instead
  of evaluating only one fixed candidate. This tests whether source-flat
  candidates are robust across surrogate choices or model-specific artifacts.

Dependencies:
  pip install numpy scipy mpmath pandas

Outputs:
  - gate1_surrogate_sweep_results.csv
  - gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv
  - optional actual-zero proxy rows if --actual-zero-proxy is used
"""

import argparse
import math
import warnings
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Callable, Dict, List, Tuple

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
from scipy.optimize import minimize_scalar
from scipy.signal import argrelextrema

try:
    import mpmath as mp
except Exception:
    mp = None

# -----------------------------
# Basic arithmetic helpers
# -----------------------------

def von_mangoldt_values(N: int) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Lambda(n) for n <= N using a simple sieve-like prime-power pass.
    """
    lam = np.zeros(N + 1, dtype=float)
    is_prime = np.ones(N + 1, dtype=bool)
    is_prime[:2] = False

    for p in range(2, N + 1):
        if is_prime[p]:
            for k in range(p * p, N + 1, p):
                is_prime[k] = False
            pk = p
            while pk <= N:
                lam[pk] = math.log(p)
                pk *= p
    return lam

def smoothing_weights(n: np.ndarray, N: int, mode: str) -> np.ndarray:
    x = n / float(N)
    if mode == "exp":
        return np.exp(-x)
    if mode == "cos":
        w = np.zeros_like(x, dtype=float)
        mask = x <= 1
        w[mask] = 0.5 * (1 + np.cos(np.pi * x[mask]))
        return w
    if mode == "sharp":
        return (x <= 1).astype(float)
    raise ValueError(f"unknown smoothing mode: {mode}")

@dataclass
class SurrogateModel:
    N: int
    smoothing: str
    level: int
    n: np.ndarray
    logn: np.ndarray
    coeff_main: np.ndarray
    coeff_dual: np.ndarray
    norm: float

    def source_value(self, t: float) -> float:
        """
        Surrogate q''_can(t) approximation.
        Level 1: main only
        Level 2: main + dual-like
        Level 3: main + dual-like + smooth background
        """
        phase = np.exp(-1j * t * self.logn)
        main = np.real(np.sum(self.coeff_main * phase))

        val = main

        if self.level >= 2:
            # A crude chi-like dual surrogate. Not a real AFE; meant for robustness testing.
            # Deterministic slowly varying phase/amplitude.
            chi_phase = np.exp(1j * (0.5 * t * np.log(max(t, 2.0) / (2 * np.pi)) - 0.5 * t))
            dual = np.real(chi_phase * np.sum(self.coeff_dual * np.conj(phase)))
            val += 0.65 * dual

        if self.level >= 3:
            # Smooth background proxy. Small and slowly varying.
            val += 0.04 * math.sin(0.7 * math.log(max(t, 2.0))) + 0.02 * math.cos(0.17 * t)

        return val / self.norm

    def derivative_value(self, t: float, r: int) -> float:
        """
        r-th t derivative of surrogate source q''_can(t), normalized.
        """
        phase = np.exp(-1j * t * self.logn)
        main = np.real(np.sum(self.coeff_main * ((-1j * self.logn) ** r) * phase))
        val = main

        if self.level >= 2:
            chi_phase = np.exp(1j * (0.5 * t * np.log(max(t, 2.0) / (2 * np.pi)) - 0.5 * t))
            # Approximate derivative: differentiate phase terms, ignore chi derivatives for this pilot.
            dual = np.real(chi_phase * np.sum(self.coeff_dual * ((1j * self.logn) ** r) * np.conj(phase)))
            val += 0.65 * dual

        if self.level >= 3:
            # Derivatives of smooth background up to a few orders; beyond that negligible for pilot.
            if r == 0:
                bg = 0.04 * math.sin(0.7 * math.log(max(t, 2.0))) + 0.02 * math.cos(0.17 * t)
            elif r == 1:
                bg = 0.04 * 0.7 * math.cos(0.7 * math.log(max(t, 2.0))) / max(t, 2.0) - 0.02 * 0.17 * math.sin(0.17 * t)
            else:
                bg = 0.02 * (0.17 ** r) * math.cos(0.17 * t + r * math.pi / 2)
            val += bg

        return val / self.norm

    def source_jets(self, t: float, R: int) -> np.ndarray:
        Q = math.log(max(t, 3.0))
        Delta = 1.0 / Q
        return np.array([(Delta ** r) * self.derivative_value(t, r) for r in range(R + 1)])

    def source_objective(self, t: float, R: int) -> float:
        jets = self.source_jets(t, R)
        return float(np.sum(jets ** 2))

    def interval_energy(self, t0: float, cI: float = 0.5, grid: int = 401) -> Tuple[float, float, float]:
        Q = math.log(max(t0, 3.0))
        half = cI / Q
        xs = np.linspace(t0 - half, t0 + half, grid)
        vals = np.array([self.source_value(float(x)) for x in xs])
        E = float(np.trapz(vals ** 2, xs) / (2 * half))
        S = float(np.max(np.abs(vals)))
        Beff = -math.log(max(E, 1e-300)) / math.log(Q)
        return E, S, Beff

def make_model(N: int, smoothing: str, level: int) -> SurrogateModel:
    lam = von_mangoldt_values(N)
    n = np.arange(2, N + 1, dtype=float)
    logn = np.log(n)
    lamn = lam[2:]

    W = smoothing_weights(n, N, smoothing)

    # Source-curvature-like weights: Lambda(n) * (log n)^2 * n^-1/2 * W.
    coeff_main = lamn * (logn ** 2) * (n ** -0.5) * W

    # Dual-like weights: reverse-ish smoothing with lower log power for diversity.
    W_dual = smoothing_weights(n, N, "cos" if smoothing != "cos" else "exp")
    coeff_dual = lamn * (logn ** 2) * (n ** -0.5) * W_dual

    # Normalize RMS over a modest sample grid so objectives compare across cutoffs.
    sample_ts = np.linspace(100.0, 800.0, 256)
    raw_vals = []
    for t in sample_ts:
        phase = np.exp(-1j * t * logn)
        raw_vals.append(np.real(np.sum(coeff_main * phase)))
    norm = float(np.sqrt(np.mean(np.array(raw_vals) ** 2)))
    norm = max(norm, 1e-12)

    return SurrogateModel(
        N=N,
        smoothing=smoothing,
        level=level,
        n=n,
        logn=logn,
        coeff_main=coeff_main,
        coeff_dual=coeff_dual,
        norm=norm,
    )

# -----------------------------
# Search
# -----------------------------

def find_local_minima_candidates(
    model: SurrogateModel,
    R: int,
    t_min: float,
    t_max: float,
    coarse_points: int,
    keep: int,
) -> List[Tuple[float, float]]:
    ts = np.linspace(t_min, t_max, coarse_points)
    vals = np.array([model.source_objective(float(t), R) for t in ts])

    # Get local minima indices, plus global best fallback.
    loc_idx = argrelextrema(vals, np.less, order=2)[0].tolist()
    loc_idx.append(int(np.argmin(vals)))
    loc_idx = sorted(set(loc_idx), key=lambda i: vals[i])[:keep]

    candidates = []
    step = (t_max - t_min) / (coarse_points - 1)

    for i in loc_idx:
        lo = max(t_min, ts[i] - 2 * step)
        hi = min(t_max, ts[i] + 2 * step)

        res = minimize_scalar(lambda x: model.source_objective(float(x), R), bounds=(lo, hi), method="bounded")
        candidates.append((float(res.x), float(res.fun)))

    candidates = sorted(candidates, key=lambda x: x[1])
    return candidates[:keep]

def run_surrogate_sweep(args) -> Tuple[pd.DataFrame, pd.DataFrame]:
    rows = []
    best_rows = []

    for N in args.cutoffs:
        for smoothing in args.smoothing:
            for level in args.levels:
                model = make_model(N=N, smoothing=smoothing, level=level)

                candidates = find_local_minima_candidates(
                    model=model,
                    R=args.R,
                    t_min=args.t_min,
                    t_max=args.t_max,
                    coarse_points=args.coarse_points,
                    keep=args.keep_candidates,
                )

                for rank, (t0, obj) in enumerate(candidates, start=1):
                    jets = model.source_jets(t0, args.R)
                    jmax = float(np.max(np.abs(jets)))

                    width_results = {}
                    for cI in args.widths:
                        E, S, Beff = model.interval_energy(t0, cI=cI, grid=args.interval_grid)
                        width_results[f"E_cI_{cI}"] = E
                        width_results[f"S_cI_{cI}"] = S
                        width_results[f"Beff_cI_{cI}"] = Beff

                    row = {
                        "N": N,
                        "smoothing": smoothing,
                        "level": level,
                        "R": args.R,
                        "rank": rank,
                        "t0": t0,
                        "source_objective": obj,
                        "J_max": jmax,
                        **width_results,
                    }
                    rows.append(row)

                if candidates:
                    t0, obj = candidates[0]
                    E, S, Beff = model.interval_energy(t0, cI=0.5, grid=args.interval_grid)
                    best_rows.append({
                        "N": N,
                        "smoothing": smoothing,
                        "level": level,
                        "R": args.R,
                        "best_t0": t0,
                        "best_objective": obj,
                        "E_cI_0.5": E,
                        "S_cI_0.5": S,
                        "Beff_cI_0.5": Beff,
                        "J_max": float(np.max(np.abs(model.source_jets(t0, args.R)))),
                    })

    return pd.DataFrame(rows), pd.DataFrame(best_rows)

# -----------------------------
# Optional actual-zero proxy cross-check
# -----------------------------

def hardy_z_zeros_near(t0: float, radius: float, step: float = 0.1, mp_dps: int = 30) -> np.ndarray:
    if mp is None:
        raise RuntimeError("mpmath not installed")
    mp.mp.dps = mp_dps

    def zval(x):
        return float(mp.siegelz(x))

    xs = np.arange(t0 - radius, t0 + radius + step, step)
    zs = []
    vals = []

    prev_x = xs[0]
    prev_v = zval(prev_x)

    for x in xs[1:]:
        v = zval(float(x))
        if prev_v == 0:
            zs.append(prev_x)
        elif v == 0 or prev_v * v < 0:
            # Linear interpolation is enough for proxy; not certified.
            root = prev_x + (float(x) - prev_x) * abs(prev_v) / (abs(prev_v) + abs(v))
            zs.append(root)
        prev_x, prev_v = float(x), v

    return np.array(zs, dtype=float)

def K2_proxy(m: np.ndarray, gamma: float, eps: float) -> np.ndarray:
    x = m - gamma
    den = x*x + eps*eps
    return 2 * eps * (3*x*x - eps*eps) / den**3

def zero_proxy_energy(t0: float, zeros: np.ndarray, cI: float = 0.5, kappa: float = 0.5, W: float = 40.0, grid: int = 401):
    Q = math.log(max(t0, 3.0))
    eps = kappa / Q
    half = cI / Q
    xs = np.linspace(t0 - half, t0 + half, grid)

    use = zeros[np.abs(zeros - t0) <= W]
    vals = np.zeros_like(xs)
    for g in use:
        vals += K2_proxy(xs, g, eps)

    E = float(np.trapz(vals**2, xs) / (2 * half))
    S = float(np.max(np.abs(vals)))
    Beff = -math.log(max(E, 1e-300)) / math.log(Q)

    return {
        "zero_proxy_E": E,
        "zero_proxy_S": S,
        "zero_proxy_Beff": Beff,
        "zero_proxy_zeros_used": len(use),
    }

def run_actual_zero_proxy_for_best(best_df: pd.DataFrame, args) -> pd.DataFrame:
    rows = []
    for _, row in best_df.head(args.proxy_best_count).iterrows():
        t0 = float(row["best_t0"])
        try:
            zeros = hardy_z_zeros_near(t0, radius=args.proxy_radius, step=args.proxy_step, mp_dps=args.mp_dps)
            zp = zero_proxy_energy(t0, zeros, cI=0.5, kappa=0.5, W=min(40.0, args.proxy_radius), grid=401)
            rows.append({
                **row.to_dict(),
                "proxy_zero_count": len(zeros),
                "proxy_zero_min": float(np.min(zeros)) if len(zeros) else np.nan,
                "proxy_zero_max": float(np.max(zeros)) if len(zeros) else np.nan,
                **zp,
            })
        except Exception as e:
            rows.append({
                **row.to_dict(),
                "proxy_error": repr(e),
            })
    return pd.DataFrame(rows)

# -----------------------------
# Main
# -----------------------------

def parse_args():
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser()
    p.add_argument("--t-min", type=float, default=80.0)
    p.add_argument("--t-max", type=float, default=4000.0)
    p.add_argument("--coarse-points", type=int, default=4000)
    p.add_argument("--keep-candidates", type=int, default=3)
    p.add_argument("--R", type=int, default=8)
    p.add_argument("--cutoffs", type=int, nargs="+", default=[200, 350, 500, 800])
    p.add_argument("--smoothing", nargs="+", default=["exp", "cos", "sharp"])
    p.add_argument("--levels", type=int, nargs="+", default=[1, 2, 3])
    p.add_argument("--widths", type=float, nargs="+", default=[0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1.0])
    p.add_argument("--interval-grid", type=int, default=401)

    p.add_argument("--actual-zero-proxy", action="store_true")
    p.add_argument("--proxy-best-count", type=int, default=6)
    p.add_argument("--proxy-radius", type=float, default=45.0)
    p.add_argument("--proxy-step", type=float, default=0.1)
    p.add_argument("--mp-dps", type=int, default=30)

    return p.parse_args()

def main():
    warnings.filterwarnings("ignore", category=RuntimeWarning)
    args = parse_args()

    print("Running surrogate sweep...")
    all_df, best_df = run_surrogate_sweep(args)

    all_df.to_csv("gate1_surrogate_sweep_results.csv", index=False)
    best_df.to_csv("gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv", index=False)

    print("\nBest candidates by model:")
    print(best_df.sort_values("best_objective").head(20).to_string(index=False))

    if args.actual_zero_proxy:
        print("\nRunning optional actual-zero proxy cross-checks for best candidates...")
        proxy_df = run_actual_zero_proxy_for_best(best_df.sort_values("best_objective"), args)
        proxy_df.to_csv("gate1_surrogate_actual_zero_proxy_crosscheck.csv", index=False)
        print(proxy_df.head(args.proxy_best_count).to_string(index=False))

    print("\nWrote:")
    print("  gate1_surrogate_sweep_results.csv")
    print("  gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv")
    if args.actual_zero_proxy:
        print("  gate1_surrogate_actual_zero_proxy_crosscheck.csv")

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

```bash
python gate1_surrogate_sweep.py \
  --R 8 \
  --cutoffs 200 350 500 800 \
  --smoothing exp cos sharp \
  --levels 1 2 3 \
  --t-min 80 \
  --t-max 4000 \
  --coarse-points 4000 \
  --keep-candidates 3
```

Then cross-check the best few against Hardy-\(Z\) proxy zeros:

```bash
python gate1_surrogate_sweep.py \
  --R 8 \

  --proxy-best-count 6 \
  --proxy-radius 45 \
```

What to look for:

| outcome | interpretation |
|---|---|
| same model repeatedly finds \(B_I^{\rm eff}\gtrsim4\) but candidates move under cutoff/smoothing | surrogate-specific cancellation |
| each cutoff/smoothing has its own reoptimized flat candidate | robust surrogate source-flatness |
| actual-zero proxy near those candidates has \(E_I\sim1\) or larger | surrogate artifact, not actual-zero warning |
| actual-zero proxy also has small \(E_I\), stable under cutoff/regularization | serious Gate 1 warning |

## Key findings

### 1. Best surrogate candidates are genuinely flat inside the surrogate

The best interval-energy candidates are:

| rank | model | \(t_0\) | \(E_{c_I=0.5}\) | \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) | \(J_{\max}\) |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 1 | \(N=350\), cos, level 1 | 3486.574 | \(6.16\times10^{-5}\) | 4.62 | \(1.47\times10^{-2}\) |
| 2 | \(N=200\), cos, level 1 | 3088.145 | \(7.54\times10^{-5}\) | 4.56 | \(2.89\times10^{-2}\) |
| 3 | \(N=800\), exp, level 3 | 3141.396 | \(1.32\times10^{-4}\) | 4.28 | \(3.38\times10^{-2}\) |
| 4 | \(N=800\), exp, level 2 | 3141.396 | \(1.33\times10^{-4}\) | 4.28 | \(3.38\times10^{-2}\) |

So the reoptimization confirms that **source-flat-looking intervals are easy to find in fixed-prime/AFE-like surrogates**. This supports the prior conclusion: generic oscillation alone does not protect Gate 1.

### 2. But the actual-zero proxy cross-checks are strongly non-flat

The six actual-zero proxy cross-checks all reject the surrogate candidates.

| surrogate candidate | surrogate \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) | actual-zero proxy \(E_I\) | actual-zero proxy \(B_I^{\rm eff}\) |
|---|---:|---:|---:|
| \(N=500\), cos, level 3, \(t_0=3250.162\) | 3.07 | \(1.05\times10^4\) | -4.43 |
| \(N=350\), cos, level 1, \(t_0=3486.574\) | 4.62 | \(1.93\times10^7\) | -7.99 |
| \(N=200\), cos, level 1, \(t_0=3088.145\) | 4.56 | \(1.02\times10^7\) | -7.75 |
| \(N=200\), cos, level 3, \(t_0=2113.996\) | 2.96 | \(4.64\times10^2\) | -3.02 |
| \(N=200\), cos, level 2, \(t_0=2113.995\) | 2.96 | \(4.60\times10^2\) | -3.01 |
| \(N=200\), sharp, level 2, \(t_0=3105.638\) | 4.18 | \(1.21\times10^4\) | -4.51 |

This is the decisive comparison: every checked actual-zero proxy has **large positive energy**, not source-flatness.

\[
\boxed{\text{No checked surrogate candidate transfers to the actual-zero proxy.}}
\]

### 3. The surrogate flatness is real but model-specific

A few patterns:

- Cos level 1 gives the strongest interval flatness, but adding level 2/3 terms weakens it substantially.
- Exp smoothing is more stable across levels, with mean \(B_I^{\rm eff}\approx3.6\), but the candidate locations move.
- Sharp smoothing produces decent candidates around \(B_I^{\rm eff}\approx4.18\), but again the actual-zero proxy rejects them.

So the surrogate phenomenon is worth studying, but it is not yet an actual-zeta warning.

## Classification

Using the validation protocol:

\[
\boxed{\text{Classification: surrogate watch only.}}
\]

Not a serious Gate 1 warning, because:

- surrogate candidates exist;
- but cutoff/smoothing/model dependence remains visible;
- and actual-zero proxy cross-checks are strongly non-flat;
- no candidate shows actual-zero interval collapse comparable to the quadrature negative control.

## Recommended next test

Run one broader **actual-zero proxy scan** around the best surrogate candidate zones, not just at the exact surrogate minimizers:

\[
t\approx2114,\quad 3088,\quad 3106,\quad 3141,\quad 3250,\quad 3487.
\]

For each zone, scan gap midpoints and random centers in a window of \(\pm 30\) to \(\pm 50\). The specific question is:

\[
\text{Do actual-zero proxy gap midpoints near surrogate-flat zones ever produce }B_I^{\rm eff}\gg 1?
\]

Current evidence says no.

_Thought for 11s_

Below is a standalone script for the next test: **actual-zero proxy zone scans around surrogate-flat candidate heights**.

It reads your surrogate best-candidate CSV, extracts top candidate \(t_0\) zones, computes Hardy-\(Z\) sign-change zero proxies with `mpmath.siegelz`, scans gap midpoints / zero ordinates / random / uniform centers, and writes result + summary CSVs.

Save as:

```bash
gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py
```

Run:

```bash
python gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py \
  --candidate-csv gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv \
  --top 8 \
  --radius 45 \
  --step 0.1
```

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Gate 1 actual-zero proxy zone scan.

Purpose:
  Scan actual Hardy-Z sign-change zero proxies around surrogate-flat candidate
  zones, using the zero-kernel-only proxy:

      K2(m; gamma, eps)
        = 2 eps (3(m-gamma)^2 - eps^2) / ((m-gamma)^2 + eps^2)^3

  This is NOT the final canonical q''_can calculation. It is a pilot
  actual-zero-side proxy meant to test whether surrogate-flat zones correspond
  to actual-zero source-flat behavior.

Inputs:
  - gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv, or explicit --zones

Outputs:
  - gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.csv
  - gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_summary.csv
  - cached zero proxy files under ./zero_proxy_cache/

Dependencies:
  pip install numpy pandas mpmath
"""

import argparse
import hashlib
import json
import math
import os
from dataclasses import dataclass
from typing import Dict, List, Tuple

import numpy as np
import pandas as pd
import mpmath as mp

# -----------------------------
# Hardy Z zero proxy
# -----------------------------

def cache_key(t_center: float, radius: float, step: float, dps: int) -> str:
    s = f"{t_center:.8f}_{radius:.8f}_{step:.8f}_{dps}"
    return hashlib.sha1(s.encode()).hexdigest()[:16]

def hardy_z_zeros_near(
    t_center: float,
    radius: float,
    step: float = 0.1,
    dps: int = 30,
    cache_dir: str = "zero_proxy_cache",
    force: bool = False,
) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Find approximate critical-line zeros by sign changes of Hardy Z(t).

    This is proxy data, not verified Odlyzko-quality zero data.
    """
    os.makedirs(cache_dir, exist_ok=True)
    key = cache_key(t_center, radius, step, dps)
    path = os.path.join(cache_dir, f"zeros_{key}.json")

    if os.path.exists(path) and not force:
        with open(path, "r", encoding="utf-8") as f:
            data = json.load(f)
        return np.array(data["zeros"], dtype=float)

    mp.mp.dps = dps

    def zval(x: float) -> float:
        return float(mp.siegelz(x))

    lo = t_center - radius
    hi = t_center + radius
    xs = np.arange(lo, hi + step, step)

    zeros = []
    prev_x = float(xs[0])
    prev_v = zval(prev_x)

    for x in xs[1:]:
        x = float(x)
        v = zval(x)

        if prev_v == 0.0:
            zeros.append(prev_x)
        elif v == 0.0:
            zeros.append(x)
        elif prev_v * v < 0:
            # Bisection refinement inside the sign-change bracket.
            a, b = prev_x, x
            fa, fb = prev_v, v
            for _ in range(40):
                mid = 0.5 * (a + b)
                fm = zval(mid)
                if fa == 0:
                    b = a
                    break
                if fm == 0:
                    a = b = mid
                    break
                if fa * fm <= 0:
                    b, fb = mid, fm
                else:
                    a, fa = mid, fm
            zeros.append(0.5 * (a + b))

        prev_x, prev_v = x, v

    zeros = np.array(sorted(set(round(z, 12) for z in zeros)), dtype=float)

    with open(path, "w", encoding="utf-8") as f:
        json.dump(
            {
                "t_center": t_center,
                "radius": radius,
                "step": step,
                "dps": dps,
                "zeros": zeros.tolist(),
            },
            f,
            indent=2,
        )

    return zeros

# -----------------------------
# Zero-kernel proxy q''
# -----------------------------

def K2_proxy(m: np.ndarray, gamma: float, eps: float) -> np.ndarray:
    x = m - gamma
    den = x * x + eps * eps
    return 2.0 * eps * (3.0 * x * x - eps * eps) / (den ** 3)

def q2_zero_proxy(
    xs: np.ndarray,
    zeros: np.ndarray,
    center: float,
    W: float,
    kappa: float,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, int]:
    Q = math.log(max(center, 3.0))
    eps = kappa / Q
    use = zeros[np.abs(zeros - center) <= W]

    vals = np.zeros_like(xs, dtype=float)
    for g in use:
        vals += K2_proxy(xs, g, eps)

    return vals, len(use)

def interval_metrics(
    center: float,
    zeros: np.ndarray,
    cI: float = 0.5,
    kappa: float = 0.5,
    W: float = 40.0,
    grid: int = 401,
) -> Dict[str, float]:
    Q = math.log(max(center, 3.0))
    half = cI / Q
    xs = np.linspace(center - half, center + half, grid)

    vals, n_used = q2_zero_proxy(xs, zeros, center, W=W, kappa=kappa)
    E = float(np.trapz(vals ** 2, xs) / (2.0 * half))
    S = float(np.max(np.abs(vals)))
    Beff = -math.log(max(E, 1e-300)) / math.log(Q)

    return {
        "E": E,
        "S": S,
        "Beff": Beff,
        "zeros_used": n_used,
    }

def finite_jet_proxy(
    center: float,
    zeros: np.ndarray,
    R: int = 4,
    kappa: float = 0.5,
    W: float = 40.0,
    h_factor: float = 0.015,
    n_fit: int = 31,
) -> Dict[str, float]:
    """
    Estimate normalized finite jets J_r = Delta^r d^r q2/dm^r(center)
    by local polynomial fitting.

    This is diagnostic only; high-order jet estimates are noisy.
    """
    Q = math.log(max(center, 3.0))
    Delta = 1.0 / Q
    h = h_factor / Q

    xs = center + np.linspace(-h, h, n_fit)
    vals, _ = q2_zero_proxy(xs, zeros, center, W=W, kappa=kappa)

    deg = min(max(R + 2, 6), n_fit - 1)
    # Fit in local variable y = x - center for numerical conditioning.
    y = xs - center
    coeff = np.polyfit(y, vals, deg=deg)  # descending powers

    jets = []
    p = np.poly1d(coeff)
    for r in range(R + 1):
        deriv = np.polyder(p, m=r)
        raw = float(deriv(0.0))
        jets.append((Delta ** r) * raw)

    jets = np.array(jets, dtype=float)
    return {
        "J_max": float(np.max(np.abs(jets))),
        "J_0": float(jets[0]),
        "J_1": float(jets[1]) if len(jets) > 1 else np.nan,
        "J_2": float(jets[2]) if len(jets) > 2 else np.nan,
        "J_3": float(jets[3]) if len(jets) > 3 else np.nan,
        "J_4": float(jets[4]) if len(jets) > 4 else np.nan,
    }

# -----------------------------
# Center generation
# -----------------------------

def gram_theta(t: float) -> float:
    """
    Riemann-Siegel theta approximation via mpmath.
    """
    return float(mp.siegeltheta(t))

def gram_points_near(lo: float, hi: float, dps: int = 30) -> np.ndarray:
    """
    Approximate Gram points by solving theta(t) = n*pi.
    Uses coarse bracketing based on sampled theta.
    """
    mp.mp.dps = dps

    # Determine n range.
    n_lo = math.floor(gram_theta(lo) / math.pi) - 2
    n_hi = math.ceil(gram_theta(hi) / math.pi) + 2

    gps = []
    for n in range(n_lo, n_hi + 1):
        target = n * math.pi

        # Find rough bracket by local scan.
        xs = np.linspace(lo, hi, 300)
        vals = np.array([gram_theta(float(x)) - target for x in xs])
        idxs = np.where(vals[:-1] * vals[1:] <= 0)[0]
        if len(idxs) == 0:
            continue

        i = idxs[0]
        a, b = float(xs[i]), float(xs[i + 1])
        fa = gram_theta(a) - target

        for _ in range(40):
            mid = 0.5 * (a + b)
            fm = gram_theta(mid) - target
            if fa * fm <= 0:
                b = mid
            else:
                a, fa = mid, fm
        g = 0.5 * (a + b)
        if lo <= g <= hi:
            gps.append(g)

    return np.array(sorted(set(round(g, 12) for g in gps)), dtype=float)

def build_centers_for_zone(
    zeros: np.ndarray,
    zone_center: float,
    radius: float,
    random_count: int = 80,
    uniform_count: int = 120,
    seed: int = 0,
    include_gram: bool = True,
) -> List[Tuple[str, float]]:
    lo, hi = zone_center - radius, zone_center + radius
    centers = []

    z = zeros[(zeros >= lo) & (zeros <= hi)]
    for g in z:
        centers.append(("zero_ordinate", float(g)))

    if len(z) >= 2:
        mids = 0.5 * (z[:-1] + z[1:])
        gaps = z[1:] - z[:-1]

        for m in mids:
            centers.append(("gap_midpoint", float(m)))

        # Top quartile gap midpoints.
        thresh = np.quantile(gaps, 0.75)
        for m, gap in zip(mids, gaps):
            if gap >= thresh:
                centers.append(("large_gap_midpoint", float(m)))

        # Bottom quartile gap midpoints.
        sthresh = np.quantile(gaps, 0.25)
        for m, gap in zip(mids, gaps):
            if gap <= sthresh:
                centers.append(("small_gap_midpoint", float(m)))

    rng = np.random.default_rng(seed)
    for m in rng.uniform(lo, hi, size=random_count):
        centers.append(("random", float(m)))

    for m in np.linspace(lo, hi, uniform_count):
        centers.append(("uniform", float(m)))

    if include_gram:
        try:
            gps = gram_points_near(lo, hi)
            for g in gps:
                centers.append(("gram_point", float(g)))
        except Exception as e:
            print(f"WARNING: Gram point generation failed near {zone_center}: {e}")

    # Deduplicate by rounded center and family.
    seen = set()
    out = []
    for fam, c in centers:
        key = (fam, round(c, 9))
        if key not in seen and lo <= c <= hi:
            seen.add(key)
            out.append((fam, c))

    return out

# -----------------------------
# Candidate loading
# -----------------------------

def load_zones(args) -> List[float]:
    zones = []

    if args.zones:
        zones.extend(args.zones)

    if args.candidate_csv:
        df = pd.read_csv(args.candidate_csv)

        # Try common columns.
        t_col = None
        for col in ["best_t0", "t0", "candidate_t0"]:
            if col in df.columns:
                t_col = col
                break
        if t_col is None:
            raise ValueError(f"No t0 column found in {args.candidate_csv}")

        sort_col = None
        for col in ["E_cI_0.5", "best_objective", "source_objective", "J_max"]:
            if col in df.columns:
                sort_col = col
                break

        if sort_col:
            df = df.sort_values(sort_col, ascending=True)

        zones.extend([float(x) for x in df[t_col].head(args.top).tolist()])

    # Deduplicate nearby zones.
    zones_sorted = []
    for z in sorted(zones):
        if not zones_sorted or abs(z - zones_sorted[-1]) > args.merge_distance:
            zones_sorted.append(z)

    return zones_sorted

# -----------------------------
# Main scan
# -----------------------------

def scan_zone(zone: float, args) -> Tuple[pd.DataFrame, Dict]:
    zeros = hardy_z_zeros_near(
        zone,
        radius=args.zero_radius,
        step=args.zero_step,
        dps=args.mp_dps,
        cache_dir=args.cache_dir,
        force=args.force_zero_rescan,
    )

    centers = build_centers_for_zone(
        zeros=zeros,
        zone_center=zone,
        radius=args.scan_radius,
        random_count=args.random_count,
        uniform_count=args.uniform_count,
        seed=args.seed,
        include_gram=not args.no_gram,
    )

    rows = []
    for fam, center in centers:
        for cI in args.cI:
            base = {
                "zone": zone,
                "family": fam,
                "center": center,
                "cI": cI,
                "Q": math.log(max(center, 3.0)),
                "zero_count_zone": len(zeros),
                "zero_min": float(np.min(zeros)) if len(zeros) else np.nan,
                "zero_max": float(np.max(zeros)) if len(zeros) else np.nan,
            }

            metrics = interval_metrics(
                center,
                zeros,
                cI=cI,
                kappa=args.kappa,
                W=args.W,
                grid=args.grid,
            )
            jets = finite_jet_proxy(
                center,
                zeros,
                R=args.R,
                kappa=args.kappa,
                W=args.W,
                h_factor=args.jet_h_factor,
                n_fit=args.jet_fit_points,
            )

            # Stability checks for selected small subset only: all rows get W/kappa drift.
            E_base = metrics["E"]

            tail_E = []
            for W2 in args.stability_W:
                tail_E.append(interval_metrics(center, zeros, cI=cI, kappa=args.kappa, W=W2, grid=args.grid)["E"])
            tail_drift = max(abs(e - E_base) for e in tail_E) / max(abs(E_base), 1e-300)

            reg_E = []
            for k2 in args.stability_kappa:
                reg_E.append(interval_metrics(center, zeros, cI=cI, kappa=k2, W=args.W, grid=args.grid)["E"])
            reg_drift = max(abs(e - E_base) for e in reg_E) / max(abs(E_base), 1e-300)

            row = {
                **base,
                **metrics,
                **jets,
                "tail_drift": tail_drift,
                "reg_drift": reg_drift,
            }
            rows.append(row)

    meta = {
        "zone": zone,
        "zero_count": len(zeros),
        "center_count": len(centers),
    }
    return pd.DataFrame(rows), meta

def summarize_results(df: pd.DataFrame) -> pd.DataFrame:
    if df.empty:
        return pd.DataFrame()

    idx = df.groupby(["zone", "family", "cI"])["E"].idxmin()
    summary = df.loc[idx].copy()
    summary = summary.sort_values(["zone", "E"], ascending=[True, True])
    return summary

def classify_row(row, warn_Beff=3.0, serious_Beff=6.0, max_tail_drift=0.1):
    if row["tail_drift"] > max_tail_drift:
        return "reject_tail_unstable"
    if row["Beff"] >= serious_Beff and row["J_max"] < 1e-2:
        return "serious_warning_proxy"
    if row["Beff"] >= warn_Beff:
        return "watch_proxy"
    return "healthy_proxy"

def parse_args():
    p = argparse.ArgumentParser()

    p.add_argument("--candidate-csv", default="gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv")
    p.add_argument("--zones", type=float, nargs="*", default=[])
    p.add_argument("--top", type=int, default=8)
    p.add_argument("--merge-distance", type=float, default=5.0)

    p.add_argument("--zero-radius", type=float, default=55.0)
    p.add_argument("--scan-radius", type=float, default=35.0)
    p.add_argument("--zero-step", type=float, default=0.1)
    p.add_argument("--mp-dps", type=int, default=30)
    p.add_argument("--cache-dir", default="zero_proxy_cache")
    p.add_argument("--force-zero-rescan", action="store_true")

    p.add_argument("--cI", type=float, nargs="+", default=[0.1, 0.2, 0.5, 1.0])
    p.add_argument("--kappa", type=float, default=0.5)
    p.add_argument("--W", type=float, default=40.0)
    p.add_argument("--grid", type=int, default=401)

    p.add_argument("--R", type=int, default=4)
    p.add_argument("--jet-h-factor", type=float, default=0.015)
    p.add_argument("--jet-fit-points", type=int, default=31)

    p.add_argument("--random-count", type=int, default=80)
    p.add_argument("--uniform-count", type=int, default=120)
    p.add_argument("--seed", type=int, default=0)
    p.add_argument("--no-gram", action="store_true")

    p.add_argument("--stability-W", type=float, nargs="+", default=[10.0, 20.0, 40.0])
    p.add_argument("--stability-kappa", type=float, nargs="+", default=[0.25, 0.5, 1.0])

    p.add_argument("--out", default="gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.csv")
    p.add_argument("--summary-out", default="gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_summary.csv")

    return p.parse_args()

def main():
    args = parse_args()
    zones = load_zones(args)

    if not zones:
        raise RuntimeError("No zones supplied. Use --candidate-csv or --zones.")

    print(f"Scanning {len(zones)} zones:")
    for z in zones:
        print(f"  {z:.6f}")

    all_rows = []
    metas = []

    for i, zone in enumerate(zones, start=1):
        print(f"\n[{i}/{len(zones)}] Zone {zone:.6f}")
        df_zone, meta = scan_zone(zone, args)
        metas.append(meta)
        all_rows.append(df_zone)

        if not df_zone.empty:
            best = df_zone.sort_values("E").head(5)
            print(best[["family", "center", "cI", "E", "S", "Beff", "J_max", "tail_drift", "reg_drift"]].to_string(index=False))

    df = pd.concat(all_rows, ignore_index=True) if all_rows else pd.DataFrame()
    if not df.empty:
        df["classification"] = df.apply(classify_row, axis=1)

    summary = summarize_results(df)
    if not summary.empty:
        summary["classification"] = summary.apply(classify_row, axis=1)

    df.to_csv(args.out, index=False)
    summary.to_csv(args.summary_out, index=False)

    print("\nWrote:")
    print(f"  {args.out}")
    print(f"  {args.summary_out}")

    print("\nBest overall rows:")
    if not df.empty:
        print(df.sort_values("E").head(20)[
            ["zone", "family", "center", "cI", "E", "S", "Beff", "J_max", "tail_drift", "reg_drift", "classification"]
        ].to_string(index=False))

    print("\nZone metadata:")
    print(pd.DataFrame(metas).to_string(index=False))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

Recommended first run:

```bash
python gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py \
  --candidate-csv gate1_surrogate_best_candidates.csv \
  --top 8 \
  --zero-radius 55 \
  --scan-radius 35 \
  --zero-step 0.1 \
  --cI 0.1 0.2 0.5 1.0 \
  --R 4
```

Faster smoke test:

```bash
python gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py \
  --zones 2114 3088 3141 3250 3487 \
  --zero-radius 35 \
  --scan-radius 20 \
  --zero-step 0.15 \
  --random-count 20 \
  --uniform-count 40 \
  --no-gram
```

What to look for in `gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_summary.csv`:

| column | meaning |
|---|---|
| `E` | proxy interval energy |
| `Beff` | effective flatness exponent |
| `J_max` | finite-jet proxy max |
| `tail_drift` | cutoff sensitivity |
| `reg_drift` | smoothing sensitivity |
| `classification` | automatic rough label |

Interpretation:

- `healthy_proxy`: no source-flat warning.
- `watch_proxy`: worth rerunning with higher precision / better zeros.
- `serious_warning_proxy`: only meaningful if tail drift is low and the result persists across widths.
- `reject_tail_unstable`: discard.

## What thresholds to watch

Treat as healthy if:

\[
E_I \gtrsim 10^{-1},\quad B_I^{\rm eff}<1.5.
\]

Treat as watch if:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\ge 3
\]

and the result is tail-stable.

Treat as serious only if all are true:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\ge 6,\qquad J_{\max}\ll1,\qquad D_{\rm tail}<0.1,
\]

and it persists across at least two widths \(c_I\).

Given the last run’s best value was only:

\[
B_I^{\rm eff}\approx0.66,
\]

Round 2 is mainly testing whether higher height or denser center sampling changes the picture.

## `gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py`

Status: **good to run.**

What checked out:

- The \(Q\) convention is now consistently using

\[
Q=\log(m/(2\pi))
\]

inside the actual-zero proxy metrics, jet proxy, and skip logic. Centers with \(Q\le1\) are skipped in `scan_zone`, which is the right guard for `B_eff = -log(E)/log(Q)`. 

- The schema renames are applied consistently in the core scan path: `center_type`, `m0`, `c_I`, `W_factor`, `nquad`, `R_jet`, `B_eff`, `local_zero_count`, `tail_drift_rel`, `quad_drift_rel`, and `status` are used in row construction, printed best rows, and summary classification. 

- The CLI rename set is internally consistent: `--c-I-values`, `--W-factor`, `--nquad`, `--R-jet`, and `--stability-nquad` map to the names used by `scan_zone` and `compute_param_hash`. 

- Multiprocessing compatibility looks sound: `_scan_zone_worker` reconstructs `argparse.Namespace(**args_dict)` and forces `ns.workers = 1`, so multi-zone parallelism will not create nested pools. 

- `with_hash_suffix()` now produces `root.<hash>.csv`, and the param-hash key list uses the renamed attributes, so resume/hash separation should work with the new schema. 

Small recommendations:

1. **Resume edge case:** `open_resume_state()` treats a zone as complete if any rows for that zone exist. If a run is killed mid-write, a partial zone could be skipped on resume. Low probability because writes happen per-zone, but for safety you could add a `rows_per_zone` sanity check or write each zone to a temp file then append.

2. **Status thresholds are intentionally strict:** `quad_tol=1e-5` may mark some otherwise healthy high-curvature rows as `reject_quad_unstable` when changing `nquad` from 201 to 801. That is okay for candidate validation, but expect many rejects near zero ordinates. Don’t treat that as a script failure.

3. **Old CLI commands will break:** any old invocation using `--cI`, `--W`, `--grid`, or `--R` needs to be updated. Your new names are better; just make sure runbooks are updated.

## `gate1_surrogate_sweep.py`

Status: **good to run.**

What checked out:

- BLAS/OpenMP thread pinning is set before NumPy/SciPy imports, which should prevent the earlier process/thread oversubscription issue. 

- The main Gate 1 scaling now uses

\[
Q=\log(t/(2\pi))
\]

in `source_jets()`, `interval_energy()`, and the optional zero-proxy energy calculation. 

- Output paths are centralized under `scripts/zeta_bridge_agent2/out/`, and logging is timestamped. 

- You correctly left surrogate aggregate columns like `E_cI_0.5` unchanged; that avoids disrupting existing comparison tables. 

Small recommendations:

1. **Add a low-height guard here too.** The default `t_min=80` is safe, but if someone runs with low \(t\), `Q = log(t/(2π))` can be \(\le1\). Add this in `find_local_minima_candidates()` or `source_jets()`:

```python
if t <= 2.0 * math.pi * math.e:
    return np.full(R + 1, np.nan)
```

or simply validate `--t-min > 2πe`.

2. **Background term still uses `log(max(t, 2.0))`.** That is not a bug if the background is just a smooth surrogate term. If you intended every logarithmic scale in the surrogate to use \(t/(2\pi)\), then change the Level 3 background too. If the background is arbitrary smooth noise, leave it.

3. **Optional zero-proxy cross-check in this script is older than the zone-scan script.** It still returns columns like `zero_proxy_Beff` and uses the simpler Hardy-Z zero locator. That is fine as a quick check, but for serious proxy work the updated `gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py` is now the authoritative tool.

- `gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py`: `scan_zone(100)` with tiny radius/no Gram generated a valid DataFrame.
- `gate1_surrogate_sweep.py`: small `N=50`, one-level surrogate sweep generated valid result/best-candidate DataFrames.
- Both files parse/import cleanly.

\[

\]

Use the updated actual-zero scanner for all serious proxy scans, and use the surrogate sweep only to generate/reoptimize candidate zones. The only change I would make before a long run is adding the low-height \(Q>1\) guard to `gate1_surrogate_sweep.py`.

\boxed{\text{Almost ready, but fix the }W\text{-factor cutoff mismatch first.}}
\]

Both scripts parse cleanly by static AST check. The surrogate script’s low-height guard and \(Q=\log(t/(2\pi))\) changes are in. The actual-zero scanner’s schema rename, \(Q\)-guard, hash suffix, status taxonomy, `tail_edge`, and `quad_drift_rel` changes are also in.  

## Fix needed: `W_factor` is used inconsistently

In `gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.py`, `tail_edge` assumes the cutoff window is

\[
W_{\rm abs}=\frac{W_{\rm factor}}{Q},
\]

matching your change notes. But `q2_zero_proxy()` still uses `W_factor` as an **absolute** window:

```python
use = zeros[np.abs(zeros - center) <= W]
```

So with default `W_factor=40` and \(Q\approx 6\)–\(9\), the actual kernel uses a cutoff of about **40 height units**, while `tail_edge` only checks for about **40/Q ≈ 4–7 height units**. This can incorrectly mark edge-zone rows as safe even though the actual computation may need zeros outside the cached range.

Your change notes explicitly describe the edge guard as using \(W=W_{\rm factor}/Q\), so I would make the whole script use factor semantics. 

### Patch

Change `q2_zero_proxy()` to this:

```python
def q2_zero_proxy(
    xs: np.ndarray,
    zeros: np.ndarray,
    center: float,
    W_factor: float,
    kappa: float,
) -> Tuple[np.ndarray, int]:
    Q = math.log(center / (2.0 * math.pi))
    eps = kappa / Q
    W_abs = W_factor / Q
    use = zeros[np.abs(zeros - center) <= W_abs]

    vals = np.zeros_like(xs, dtype=float)
    for g in use:
        vals += K2_proxy(xs, g, eps)

    return vals, len(use)
```

Then update calls from:

```python
q2_zero_proxy(xs, zeros, center, W=W_factor, kappa=kappa)
```

to:

```python
q2_zero_proxy(xs, zeros, center, W_factor=W_factor, kappa=kappa)
```

and similarly in `finite_jet_proxy()`.

No other logic needs to change; your `tail_edge` computation is already aligned with this factor interpretation.

## Minor optional hardening

### 1. Resume safety comment is too strong

`write_zone()` says a single regular-file write + fsync makes the file “unchanged” if interrupted. That is not guaranteed for normal files. Since only the main process writes, the practical risk is low, but an interrupted write can still leave a partial zone and resume may skip it by `zone`.

Best hardening: add a `zone_complete` manifest or write each zone to a temp CSV and append only after success. Not urgent for normal runs, but the comment overstates atomicity.

### 2. Surrogate background still uses `log(max(t,2.0))`

This is fine if it is intentionally an arbitrary smooth background proxy. If you want every logarithmic scale to use the \(t/(2\pi)\) convention, change the Level 3 background too. I would leave it unless you want stricter semantic uniformity.

## Surrogate script status

`gate1_surrogate_sweep.py` looks good. The low-height guard is now explicit:

\[
t>2\pi e
\]

and `source_objective()` returns `inf` for invalid low-height jets, so the optimizer will not select bad low-\(Q\) points. 

## Final recommendation

Apply the `W_factor/Q` patch in `q2_zero_proxy()` before the next long actual-zero scan.

After that:

\[
\boxed{\text{ready to run.}}
\]

## Agent 2 / B — Canonical zero-side upgrade

### Task

I am pivoting from the completed singular-control work to the canonicalization upgrade. The current proxy

\[
q''_{\zero,\varepsilon}(m)=\sum_\gamma K_2(m;\gamma,\varepsilon)
\]

is useful for pilot scans, but it is not yet the canonical object. The target is

\[
q''_{\can}(t)=B_2(t)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(t;\rho),
\]

with exact gamma/background, canonical treatment of critical-line zeros, and a regularized tail. The latest coordinator instruction explicitly identifies this as the decisive next fidelity step. 

---

# 1. Exact gamma/background term \(B_2(t)\)

Use the completed zeta gamma phase, i.e. the Riemann–Siegel theta contribution

\[
\theta(t)
=
\Im\log\Gamma\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)
-\frac{t}{2}\log\pi.
\]

Then

\[
\theta'(t)
=
\frac12\Re \psi\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)
-\frac12\log\pi,
\]

where \(\psi\) is the digamma function.

The canonical background curvature contribution to

\[
q''_{\can}=\Phi_\zeta'''
\]

is

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18
\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
}
\]

Asymptotically,

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)= -\frac{1}{2t^2}+O(t^{-4}).
}
\]

So the earlier proxy

\[
B_2(t)\approx -\frac{1}{2t^2}
\]

is very accurate even at moderate heights.

For the watch intervals:

| \(m_0\) | exact \(B_2(m_0)\) | \(-1/(2m_0^2)\) | ratio |
|---:|---:|---:|---:|
| 27.7179 | \(-6.5101\times10^{-4}\) | \(-6.5080\times10^{-4}\) | 1.00033 |
| 109.099 | \(-4.2009\times10^{-5}\) | \(-4.2008\times10^{-5}\) | 1.00002 |
| 171.662 | \(-1.6968\times10^{-5}\) | \(-1.6968\times10^{-5}\) | 1.00001 |
| 199.640 | \(-1.2545\times10^{-5}\) | \(-1.2545\times10^{-5}\) | 1.00001 |

Conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
+B_2^{\rm exact}\text{ will not materially change existing watch intervals.}
}
\]

The main fidelity issue is **not** \(B_2\). It is the critical-line zero treatment and tail regularization.

---

# 2. Critical-line zero treatment

The current proxy replaces every critical-line zero by a smoothed Lorentzian scale

\[
c=0\rightsquigarrow \varepsilon=\kappa/Q,
\]

and then uses

\[
K_2(m;\gamma,\varepsilon)
=
\frac{2\varepsilon(3(m-\gamma)^2-\varepsilon^2)}
{\left((m-\gamma)^2+\varepsilon^2\right)^3}.
\]

This is best interpreted as a **Poisson-smoothed zero-density proxy**, not the literal canonical phase curvature.

The observed \(\kappa\)-dependence is therefore expected:

\[
\varepsilon=\kappa/Q
\]

is an artificial smoothing scale. If \(E_I\) changes materially with \(\kappa\), that does not necessarily indicate real source-curvature behavior. It may just indicate that the proxy is measuring a smoothed zero-counting curvature.

## Recommended canonical numerical treatment

Define an explicitly smoothed canonical family:

\[
q''_{\can,\eta}(t)
:=
B_2(t)+\sum_\rho^{\rm sym/reg}K_2(t;\rho,\eta),
\]

where \(\eta>0\) is not hidden as an ad hoc replacement, but declared as a **Poisson height** or **off-line evaluation height**.

For critical-line zeros \(\rho=\frac12+i\gamma\), use

\[
K_{2,\eta}(t;\gamma)
=
\partial_t^2
\left(
\frac{\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\right)
=
\frac{2\eta(3(t-\gamma)^2-\eta^2)}
{\left((t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2\right)^3}.
\]

Then test stability as

\[
\eta=\frac{\kappa}{Q},
\qquad
\kappa\in\{0.0625,0.125,0.25,0.5,1,2\}.
\]

Do **not** classify any interval as serious unless it is stable across \(\eta\). This is exactly where the current proxy can produce artifacts.

---

# 3. Regularized tail proposal

The raw sum over \(K_2\) should not be trusted with an arbitrary finite window unless there is a symmetric cutoff and a tail correction.

A practical staged tail upgrade:

## Stage T0 — current local cutoff

\[
q''_{W,\eta}(t)
=
B_2(t)+
\sum_{|\gamma-t|\le W_{\rm abs}}
K_{2,\eta}(t;\gamma).
\]

This is the current proxy.

## Stage T1 — symmetric expanding cutoff

Run:

\[
W_{\rm abs}=\frac{W_{\rm factor}}{Q},
\qquad
W_{\rm factor}\in\{10,20,40,80,160\}.
\]

Accept only if

\[
D_{\tail}
=
\frac{|E(W_2)-E(W_1)|}{\max(E(W_1),10^{-300})}
\]

is small.

## Stage T2 — smooth cutoff

Use a smooth even cutoff

\[
\chi_W(u)=\chi(u/W_{\rm abs}),
\]

with \(\chi=1\) on \(|u|\le1\) and \(\chi=0\) on \(|u|\ge2\):

\[
q''_{W,\eta,\chi}(t)
=
B_2(t)+
\sum_\gamma
\chi_W(\gamma-t)K_{2,\eta}(t;\gamma).
\]

Compare hard versus smooth cutoff.

## Stage T3 — density-tail correction

Approximate the omitted tail by integrating the mean zero density

\[
dN(\gamma)\approx \frac{1}{2\pi}\log\frac{\gamma}{2\pi}\,d\gamma.
\]

So add

\[
T_{\rm dens}(t)
=
\int_{|\gamma-t|>W_{\rm abs}}
K_{2,\eta}(t;\gamma)
\frac{1}{2\pi}\log\frac{\gamma}{2\pi}\,d\gamma
\]

with symmetric principal regularization.

This gives a controlled way to determine whether finite-window effects are creating low-energy artifacts.

---

# 4. Component-by-component expected table

For each watch interval

\[
m_0\in\{27.7179,\ 109.099,\ 171.662,\ 199.640\},
\]

run the following table:

| stage | formula | expected effect |
|---|---|---|
| proxy only | \(\sum K_{2,\eta}\) | baseline low-energy watch behavior |
| \(+B_2^{\rm exact}\) | \(B_2+\sum K_{2,\eta}\) | negligible change; \(B_2\ll\) local zero-kernel size |
| canonical critical-line smoothing sweep | vary \(\eta=\kappa/Q\) | decisive: if watch disappears, it was smoothing artifact |
| symmetric/smooth tail | vary hard/smooth \(W\) | should be stable if local |
| density-tail correction | add \(T_{\rm dens}\) | should be small; flags finite-window artifacts |

The classification rule:

\[
\boxed{
\text{If a watch interval changes mainly under }B_2,\text{ something is wrong.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If it changes under }\kappa,\text{ it is a critical-line smoothing artifact.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If it changes under }W,\text{ it is tail/cutoff artifact.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{If it survives all stages, it becomes a serious zero-side candidate.}
}
\]

---

# 5. Immediate diagnosis of known watch intervals

The known watch intervals are all likely gap-midpoint effects rather than true source-flat candidates.

Reason: the low-energy points occur at midpoints between zero ordinates. In the current proxy, the nearest critical-line zeros contribute opposite curvature tails that can partially cancel. The value is very sensitive to

\[
\eta=\kappa/Q.
\]

That is precisely the signature of proxy smoothing, not canonical source-flatness.

So my prior expectation is:

\[
\boxed{
m_0\approx27.7179,\ 109.099,\ 171.662,\ 199.640
\text{ will weaken or disappear under }\eta\text{-sweeps.}
}
\]

But this must be confirmed by the component table.

---

# 6. Suggested implementation patch

Add exact \(B_2\):

```python
import mpmath as mp

def B2_exact(t: float, dps: int = 50) -> float:
    mp.mp.dps = dps
    z = mp.mpf("0.25") + 0.5j * t
    return float(-mp.re(mp.polygamma(2, z)) / 8.0)
```

Then change interval evaluation to:

```python
vals = np.zeros_like(xs)
for g in use:
    vals += K2_proxy(xs, g, eps)

if include_B2:
    vals += np.array([B2_exact(float(x), dps=mp_dps) for x in xs])
```

For speed, use the asymptotic version unless \(t<50\):

```python
def B2_fast(t: float) -> float:
    if t > 50:
        return -0.5 / (t*t)
    return B2_exact(t)
```

Given the exact/asymptotic ratios above, this is safe for the watch intervals except possibly \(t\approx27.7\), where exact is still easy.

---

# 7. Deliverable table template

Use this for each watch interval:

| \(m_0\) | stage | \(\kappa\) | \(W_{\rm factor}\) | cutoff | \(E_I\) | \(B_{\rm eff}\) | \(S_I\) | \(J_{\max}\) | \(D_{\tail}\) | verdict |
|---:|---|---:|---:|---|---:|---:|---:|---:|---:|---|

Stage labels:

- `proxy_only`
- `plus_B2_exact`
- `eta_sweep`
- `smooth_tail`
- `density_tail`

Verdicts:

- `artifact_B2` — should almost never happen;
- `artifact_eta`;
- `artifact_tail`;
- `watch_persistent`;
- `candidate_persistent`.

---

# 8. Final verdict

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ is easy and essentially harmless.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The dominant canonicalization issue is critical-line smoothing.}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\text{The next decisive test is an }\eta\text{-sweep plus tail-regularization sweep on known watch intervals.}
}
\]

If the low-energy intervals survive that, they become real zero-side candidates. If they disappear, they were artifacts of the current \(\varepsilon=\kappa/Q\) proxy.

Good patch. The implementation matches the intended canonicalization step.

## What is now confirmed

- `B2_exact(t)` implements

\[
B_2(t)=-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right)
\]

using `mp.polygamma(2, z)`.

\[
-\frac{1}{2t^2}
\]

above \(t>50\), which is appropriate for the current pilot.

  - \(B_2\) is harmless.
  - \(\kappa\)-smoothing dominates the low-energy watch behavior.
  - Prior watch intervals are rejected as proxy artifacts / unstable, not promoted as Gate 1 candidates.

## One small semantic issue to fix

The docstring/comment in `q2_zero_proxy()` now says:

```python
q''_can,eta(t) = B_2(t) + sum ...
```

I would soften that. This is still not actually canonical because the critical-line zero contribution is still \(\eta\)-regularized by hand and the tail is not fully completed/regularized. Better wording:

```python
"""Canonical-shape smoothed proxy:
q''_{proxy,eta}(t) = B_2(t) + sum_{|gamma-t|<=W_abs} K2(t; gamma, eps).

This includes the canonical gamma curvature term B_2 but still uses an
eta-regularized critical-line zero proxy and finite local cutoff.
"""
```

That avoids accidentally overstating the status of the computation.

## On the proposed next test

Yes: **wire T2/T3 next**, but I would do it in this order:

1. **T2 smooth cutoff** first. This is easy and directly addresses `artifact_tail`.
2. **T3 density-tail correction** second. This is more model-dependent, so treat it as exploratory unless the smooth cutoff still leaves ambiguous candidates.

For T2, add a cutoff mode:

\[
\chi(u)=
\begin{cases}
1,& |u|\le 1,\\
\frac12\left(1+\cos \pi(|u|-1)\right),&1<|u|<2,\\
0,& |u|\ge2.
\end{cases}
\]

with \(u=(\gamma-m)/W_{\rm abs}\), and compare `cutoff=hard` vs `cutoff=smooth`.

Current result is already strong enough to say:

\[
\boxed{\text{the old watch intervals were not Gate 1 candidates.}}
\]

The next fidelity step is mainly to make future rejections cleaner by separating `artifact_tail` from `artifact_eta`.
