  │ 171.662 │ 5.1e-2 │ 2.49  │ 0.132      │ 1.3e-3       │ 7.51        │ 1.5e-4   │ reject_tail_unstable │
  ├─────────┼────────┼───────┼────────────┼──────────────┼─────────────┼──────────┼──────────────────────┤
  │ 199.640 │ 7.7e-2 │ 2.07  │ 0.045      │ (small)      │ 7.12        │ 9e-5     │ reject_tail_unstable │
  └─────────┴────────┴───────┴────────────┴──────────────┴─────────────┴──────────┴──────────────────────┘

  What T2 tells us

  smooth_drift_rel is 2-3 orders of magnitude smaller than tail_drift_rel for every interval (e.g. 109.099: 8.6e-4 vs 0.106 — a ratio of ~120×). That means:

  - Replacing the hard indicator χ_{|u|≤1} with the cosine taper at the same W_factor barely moves E_I.
  - Therefore the window's discontinuous edge is not the artifact source. The hard cutoff is not introducing visible Gibbs-style ringing or boundary
  discontinuity bias at these heights.
  - But tail_drift_rel (sweeping W_factor over {10, 20, 40}) is large.

  These two observations together point to the right diagnosis: it's not the shape of the window, it's which zeros get included at all. Different W_factor
  includes different sets of zeros from the unbounded sum, and those tails have meaningful curvature contribution. The truncation magnitude — not the cutoff edge
   — is what's biting.

  This is exactly the diagnostic T2 was designed to provide, and it tells us T3 (density-tail correction) is the right next step, not a different cutoff shape.

  Mapping to your prior taxonomy

  - artifact_B2: ruled out at every interval (B2_drift ≤ 0.017, all far below B2_tol = 0.5). ✓ as you predicted.
  - artifact_eta: confirmed (kappa_drift ∈ [3.04, 7.51], all ≫ kappa_tol = 0.1). ✓
  - artifact_tail_smooth: ruled out (smooth_drift ≤ 1.3e-3, all ≪ smooth_tol = 5e-2). The hard window itself isn't the problem.
  - The remaining tail dependence is magnitude-driven, which T3's density correction targets.

  Outputs:
  - out/gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_scan.c350cfbe1d23.csv (32 rows, includes smooth_drift_rel column)
  - out/gate1_actual_zero_proxy_zone_summary.c350cfbe1d23.csv

  Want me to wire T3 next — T_dens(t) = ∫_{|γ-t|>W_abs} K_2(t;γ) (1/2π) log(γ/2π) dγ with symmetric principal regularization, plus the corresponding
  density_drift_rel column? Given the cleanness of the T2 result, I'd argue it is now exploratory: the verdict ("not Gate-1 candidates, dominated by η-smoothing
  artifact") is already secure. T3 would mainly help if a future candidate passes both tail and smooth tests, to distinguish remaining magnitude-vs-density-model
   dependence.

Yes: wire **T3**, but classify it as **exploratory / future-candidate hardening**, not as necessary to reject the current watch intervals.

Your T2 result already gives a clean diagnosis:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The old watch intervals are not Gate 1 candidates.}
}
\]

Reason:

\[
D_{\kappa}\gg1
\]

at every watch interval, so the low-energy behavior is dominated by artificial \(\eta=\kappa/Q\) smoothing. The smooth-cutoff result adds that the hard cutoff edge is not the culprit:

\[
D_{\rm smooth}\ll D_{\rm tail}.
\]

So the current interval rejection is already secure.

## What T3 should do

T3 should answer a narrower question:

\[
\text{If a future interval passes }\kappa\text{-stability and smooth-cutoff stability, is remaining }W\text{-dependence explainable by mean density?}
\]

So I would add T3, but do **not** let it override the `artifact_eta` classification. Classification priority should remain:

1. `reject_tail_edge`
2. `reject_quad_unstable`
3. `artifact_eta`
4. `artifact_B2`
5. `artifact_tail_smooth`
6. `artifact_tail_density`
7. candidate/watch statuses

For the current watch intervals, T3 should only annotate, not rescue.

## Recommended T3 implementation

Add an optional density-tail correction

\[
T_{\rm dens}(t;W,\eta)
=
\int_{|\gamma-t|>W_{\rm abs}}
K_2(t;\gamma,\eta)\,
\frac{1}{2\pi}\log\frac{\gamma}{2\pi}\,d\gamma
\]

with symmetric truncation:

\[
\gamma\in[t-L,t-W_{\rm abs}]\cup[t+W_{\rm abs},t+L].
\]

Use a lower bound guard \(\gamma>2\pi\), since \(\log(\gamma/2\pi)\) changes sign below that.

For numerical stability, change variables

\[
u=\gamma-t.
\]

Then

\[
T_{\rm dens}(t;W,\eta,L)
=
\int_{W_{\rm abs}<|u|<L}
K_2(t;t+u,\eta)
\frac{1}{2\pi}\log\frac{t+u}{2\pi}\,du.
\]

Since

\[
K_2(t;t+u,\eta)
=
\frac{2\eta(3u^2-\eta^2)}{(u^2+\eta^2)^3},
\]

this is easy to integrate numerically on two tails.

## Practical defaults

Use:

```text
--include-density-tail
--density-tail-L-factor 400
--density-tail-nquad 2001
```

where

\[
L_{\rm abs}=\frac{L_{\rm factor}}{Q}.
\]

Compare density-corrected energies at:

\[
W_{\rm factor}\in\{10,20,40,80\}.
\]

Define:

\[
D_{\rm density}
=
\frac{|E_{\rm density}(W=40)-E_{\rm no\ density}(W=40)|}
{\max(E_{\rm no\ density}(W=40),10^{-300})}.
\]

and also:

\[
D_{\rm tail,density}
=
\max_W
\frac{|E_{\rm density}(W)-E_{\rm density}(40)|}
{\max(E_{\rm density}(40),10^{-300})}.
\]

The second is more important: if the density correction is doing its job, `tail_drift_rel` should drop materially after applying it.

## Stop condition

If T3 shows the current watch intervals are still \(\kappa\)-unstable, do not spend more time on them. Move to broader actual-zero scans or canonical AFE comparison.

Current conclusion remains:

\[
\boxed{
B_2\text{ harmless; hard cutoff shape harmless; old watch intervals are }\eta\text{-artifacts.}
}
\]

## Assistant (2026-04-26 19:25:08)

_Thought for 20s_

## Agent 2 / B — Final \(B_2\) implementation handoff

### 1. Exact formula

The gamma/background curvature term is

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)=\theta'''(t)
=
-\frac18\Re\psi^{(2)}\!\left(\frac14+\frac{it}{2}\right).
}
\]

Here \(\psi^{(2)}\) is the second polygamma function, i.e. the second derivative of the digamma function.

---

### 2. Recommended exact implementation

```python
import mpmath as mp

def B2_exact(t, dps=50):
    mp.mp.dps = dps
    z = mp.mpf("0.25") + 0.5j * mp.mpf(t)
    return float(-mp.re(mp.polygamma(2, z)) / 8.0)
```

For vector grids, cache by grid endpoints / length / precision, as already done in the current scanner.

---

### 3. Fast approximation

Approved leading approximation:

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)\approx-\frac{1}{2t^2}.
}
\]

Better 3-term approximation:

\[
\boxed{
B_2(t)\approx
-\frac1{2t^2}
-\frac1{8t^4}
-\frac7{64t^6}.
}
\]

Recommended policy:

```python
def B2_fast(t, dps=50):
    if t >= 50:
        return -0.5 / (t * t)
    return B2_exact(t, dps=dps)
```

If you want essentially exact numerical agreement at negligible cost, use the 3-term expansion for \(t\ge 50\):

```python
def B2_fast_3term(t, dps=50):
    if t >= 50:
        t2 = t * t
        return -1/(2*t2) - 1/(8*t2*t2) - 7/(64*t2*t2*t2)
    return B2_exact(t, dps=dps)
```

The leading term is already enough for pilot classification; the 3-term version is cheap and nearly exact at these heights.

---

### 4. Default inclusion

\[
\boxed{
B_2 \text{ should be included by default in all future zero-side proxy/canonical scans.}
}
\]

The scanner may keep a `--no-include-B2` switch only as a diagnostic to compute `B2_drift_rel`.

---

### 5. Candidate classification rule

Rows using only \(B_2\), or any diagnostic `B2_only` mode, must be excluded from Gate 1 candidate classification.

Gate 1 concerns the full object:

\[
\boxed{
q''_{\can}(m)=B_2(m)+\sum_\rho^{\rm reg}K_2(m;\rho),
}
\]

not the background term alone.

So `B2_only` rows are allowed for drift/background diagnostics only, never for `candidate_proxy_flat`, `serious_proxy_warning`, or similar Gate 1 statuses.

---

### 6. Validation table

Relative error is

\[
\frac{|B_2^{\rm approx}-B_2^{\rm exact}|}{|B_2^{\rm exact}|}.

## Agent 2 / B — Canonical critical-line treatment handoff

### Scope

\(B_2\) is frozen. The next blocker is the artificial critical-line replacement

\[
c=0\mapsto \varepsilon=\kappa/Q.
\]

The current broad proxy scans are useful, but they are still measuring an \(\eta\)-regularized proxy. The next canonical upgrade should make the smoothing/regularization explicit, reproducible, and comparable against the existing \(\kappa/Q\) sensor. The coordinator instruction correctly says Agent 2 should stop refining \(B_2\) and focus on this canonical critical-line / completed-phase treatment. 

---

# 1. Recommended canonical smoothed family

Define a declared smoothed family, not an ad hoc critical-line replacement:

\[
q''_{\can,\eta}(t)
=
B_2(t)
+
\sum_\rho^{\rm sym/reg}
K_{2,\eta}(t;\rho),
\]

where \(\eta>0\) is a stated vertical evaluation / Poisson smoothing height.

For critical-line zeros \(\rho=1/2+i\gamma\), use

\[
K_{2,\eta}(t;\gamma)
=
\partial_t^2
\left[
\frac{\eta}{(t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2}
\right]
=
\frac{2\eta(3(t-\gamma)^2-\eta^2)}
{\left((t-\gamma)^2+\eta^2\right)^3}.
\]

This is exactly the existing kernel, but the interpretation changes:

\[
\boxed{
\varepsilon=\eta\text{ is a declared smoothing parameter, not a substitute for zero depth.}
}
\]

Use

\[
\eta=\frac{\kappa}{Q},
\qquad
Q=\log\frac{t}{2\pi},
\]

only as one family of sensors.

---

# 2. Canonical comparison modes

Implement three modes.

## Mode A — existing proxy sensor

\[
\eta=\frac{\kappa}{Q},
\qquad
\kappa\in\{0.0625,0.125,0.25,0.5,1,2\}.
\]

This remains useful for detecting smoothing artifacts.

## Mode B — fixed physical \(\eta\)

Use

\[
\eta\in\{0.02,0.05,0.1,0.2\}
\]

where feasible. This checks whether low-energy behavior is tied specifically to \(\kappa/Q\).

## Mode C — scale-normalized family

For interval

\[
I=[m_0-c_I/Q,m_0+c_I/Q],
\]

set

\[
\eta=\lambda |I|
\]

with

\[
\lambda\in\{0.05,0.1,0.25,0.5,1\}.
\]

This ties smoothing to the interval actually being tested.

Classification rule:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No candidate is serious unless it survives all three smoothing modes.}
}
\]

---

# 3. Completed-phase interpretation

The canonical object should ultimately come from the completed phase, not from choosing a smoothing width around critical-line zeros. Numerically, the most honest bridge is:

\[
q''_{\can,\eta}(t)
=
\partial_t^2
\Im\log \xi\!\left(\frac12+\eta+it\right)
\]

or the equivalent completed-phase boundary value after subtracting/handling singular jumps.

Then compare it to the zero-kernel sum:

\[
B_2(t)+\sum_\rho K_{2,\eta}(t;\rho).
\]

This gives a direct consistency test:

\[
D_{\rm completed}
=
\frac{
\int_I
\left|
q''_{\can,\eta,\xi}(t)
-
q''_{\can,\eta,\zero}(t)
\right|^2dt
}{
\max\left(
\int_I|q''_{\can,\eta,\zero}(t)|^2dt,
10^{-300}
\right)
}.
\]

For a pilot, the zero-kernel family is enough. For canonical classification, a completed-phase cross-check should be added.

---

# 4. Exact implementation spec

Keep the existing \(B_2\) default.

Add CLI options:

```text
--eta-mode kappa_over_Q | fixed | interval_scaled
--eta-values ...
--completed-phase-check
```

Pseudo-function:

```python
def eta_value(center, c_I, Q, mode, value):
    if mode == "kappa_over_Q":
        return value / Q
    if mode == "fixed":
        return value
    if mode == "interval_scaled":
        interval_half_width = c_I / Q
        return value * (2.0 * interval_half_width)
    raise ValueError(mode)
```

Then replace the current `kappa` loop with a general `eta` loop:

```python
for eta_mode in eta_modes:
    for eta_param in eta_values[eta_mode]:
        eta = eta_value(center, c_I, Q, eta_mode, eta_param)
        vals = B2(xs) + zero_kernel_sum(xs, zeros, center, eta, W_factor)
        E, S, B_eff = interval_metrics(vals)
```

Keep current columns, but add:

```text
eta_mode
eta_param
eta_abs
eta_drift_rel
completed_phase_drift_rel
```

## Assistant (2026-04-26 20:19:12)

_Thought for 46s_

This checks out. The canonical / completed-phase cross-check is a material upgrade over the proxy branch and strongly validates that the proxy formula is measuring the intended smoothed completed-phase object.

## What is solid

The new `gate1_canonical_zeta_crosscheck.py` directly compares:

\[
q''_{\can,\eta}(t)=\frac{d^3}{dt^3}\Im\log\xi\left(\frac12+\eta+it\right)
\]

against the proxy:

\[
B_2(t)+\sum_{|\gamma-t|\le W_{\rm abs}}K_2(t;\gamma,\eta).
\]

The script computes the completed-phase sensor using `mpmath.zeta` and `mpmath.loggamma`, then applies a 7-point central third-derivative stencil; it compares this to the zero-side proxy on the same grid and reports \(D_{\rm completed}\) and \(E_{\zeta}/E_{\rm proxy}\). 

The agreement table is excellent. For candidate-relevant widths \(c_I\ge0.2\), the median \(D_{\rm completed}\) is typically \(10^{-4}\) or better, and for \(c_I=0.5,1.0\) it is around \(10^{-6}\). The energy ratio is generally within about \(0.1\%\)–\(0.3\%\), except for small-window random healthy rows where stencil resolution becomes the limiting factor. 

## Interpretation

This is the key conclusion:

\[
\boxed{
\text{The zero-side proxy is not merely a heuristic; it numerically matches the smoothed completed-phase sensor.}
}
\]

So the earlier proxy results are now much more meaningful:

- broad actual-zero scans found no \(B_{\rm eff}>5\);
- old watch intervals were rejected as \(\eta\)-artifacts;
- three-mode \(\eta\) tests produced no promoted candidates;
- now the completed-phase \(\xi\) sensor agrees with the proxy on the target list.

Together:

\[
\boxed{
\text{No numerical evidence against Gate 1 has appeared in the tested smoothed completed-phase regime.}
}
\]

## Caveats

The remaining caveats are manageable and correctly identified:

1. **The 8 failures are not candidate-relevant.** They occur in random healthy rows, small \(c_I\), higher \(t\), and have \(B_{\rm eff}\le0.07\). They look like third-derivative stencil resolution limits, not source-flatness. 

2. **This is still smoothed.** It validates

\[
q''_{\can,\eta}
\]

for \(\eta=\kappa/Q\), not a singular boundary-value object at \(\eta=0\). But the whole point of the current numerical branch was to test the smoothed finite-\(\eta\) sensors; on that basis, this is a pass.

3. **The code’s use of `mp.arg(mp.zeta(s))` depends on unwrap.** The script unwraps the phase grid, which is appropriate for \(\eta>0\), but if you push to much tighter grids or much higher heights, you should include a stencil convergence check with `--ngrid 401 --mp-dps-zeta 50`.

## Practical recommendation

The proxy branch is done. Do not keep refining it unless a new anomaly appears.

Next best work:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Move to theorem-side prime/AFE nonrecurrence or a higher-height completed-phase spot check.}
}
\]

For a quick numerical hardening run only, rerun the 8 failing small-window rows with:

```bash
--ngrid 401 --mp-dps-zeta 50
```

But that is only to clean the diagnostic table; it will not affect the Gate 1 conclusion.
